## Assessment report

## Kayshild

International non-proprietary name: Semaglutide

## Note

Assessment report as adopted by the CHMP with all information of a commercially confidential nature deleted.

## 1. Administrative/regulatory information and recommendations on the procedure

## 1.1. Information on the product

| Product data                                       |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
|----------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Product name                                       | Kayshild                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| Active substance                                   | Semaglutide                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| INN or common name                                 | Semaglutide                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| Applicant                                          | Novo Nordisk A/S Novo Alle 1 2880 Bagsvaerd DENMARK                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| EMA product number                                 | EMEA/H/C/006426                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| ATC code and pharmacotherapeutic group             | A10BJ06 L2: a10drugs used in diabetes, L3: a10bblood glucose lowering drugs, excl. insulins, L4: a10bj glucagon-like peptide-1 (glp-1) analogues                                                                                         |
| Pharmaceutical form(s) and strength (s)            | Solution for injection 0.25 mg, 0.5 mg, 1 mg, 1.7 mg and 2.4 mg                                                                                                                                                                          |
| Packaging                                          | cartridge (glass) in pre-filled pen (FlexTouch)                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| Package size(s)                                    | 1 pre-filled pen + 4 needles                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| Route of administration                            | Subcutaneous use                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Device or diagnostic                               | The pen-injector for semaglutide is a drug-device combination                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Orphan designation                                 | No                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Orphan indication status confirmed                 | Not applicable                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| PRIME scheme                                       | Not applied for                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| Type of marketing authorisation granted at opinion | Conditional                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| Legal basis                                        | Article 8.3 of Directive 2001/83/EC                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| Final indication                                   | Kayshild is indicated in conjunction with diet and exercise for the treatment of adults with non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunction- associated steatohepatitis (MASH) with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (fibrosis stages F2 to F3). |
| New active substance status                        | Not applied for                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |

## 1.2. Scientific advice

Table 1: Scientific advice and protocol assistance

| Date            | Topic (quality / non- clinical/ clinical)   | Reference number / Coordinator(s)   | Brief summary of the advice                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
|-----------------|---------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|

## 1.3. Eligibility to the centralised procedure

The applicant Novo Nordisk A/S submitted on 4 March 2025 an application for marketing authorisation to the European Medicines Agency (EMA) for Kayshild (semaglutide), through the centralised procedure falling within the Article 3(1) and point 1 of Annex of Regulation (EC) No 726/2004. The eligibility to the centralised procedure was agreed upon by the EMA/CHMP on 14 September 2023.

The applicant applied for the following indication: treatment of non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunctionassociated steatohepatitis (MASH) in adults with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (consistent with stages F2 to F3 fibrosis).

## 2. Introduction

## 2.1. Therapeutic context

Note: The nomenclature for fatty liver disease has undergone revisions and a new nomenclature was announced at EASL Congress 2023. The term Non-alcoholic Fatty Liver Disease (NAFLD) has been updated to Metabolic Dysfunction-Associated Steatotic Liver Disease (MASLD) and Non-alcoholic Steatohepatitis (NASH) has been updated to Metabolic Dysfunction-Associated Steatohepatitis (MASH). In line with latest consensus, the term MASH has been used throughout the document.

Non-alcoholic steatohepatitis (MASH) is a progressive liver disease, part of the spectrum of non-alcoholic fatty liver diseases (NAFLD). It is estimated that the global prevalence of NAFLD is approximately 30% and increasing, with the highest prevalence seen in South America and the Middle East. The global prevalence of MASH in the general population is estimated to be between 4% and 7%, based on data from 2019. More recent data suggest a prevalence of asymptomatic MASH of 14% in a study of middle-aged people from the US.

In approximately 20% of people with NAFLD, fatty liver disease progresses to MASH, which is characterised by the presence of hepatic steatosis in at least 5% of hepatic cells with inflammation and hepatocyte injury (also known as hepatocyte ballooning), with or without evidence of liver fibrosis. As NASH progresses, fibrosis can lead to cirrhosis, which is associated with further complications such as hepatic decompensation events, liver failure and hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC). Consequently, NASH is one of the main indications for liver transplantation in many countries. The risk of mortality in NAFLD/MASH increases with disease severity, with cardiovascular disease being the most common cause of death in people with NAFLD. MASH progression is associated with increased risk of complications, and late diagnosis of MASH is associated with higher risk of complications. In people with MASH and advanced fibrosis, liver-related events are the most frequent complication. A strong association between NAFLD/MASH and increased cardiovascular risk is recognised with cardiovascular disease being the overall most frequent complication. NAFLD/MASH and cardiovascular disease share several cardiometabolic risk factors, including obesity, T2D, metabolic syndrome, hypertension, dyslipidaemia, and chronic kidney disease (CKD).

NAFLD and MASH are closely associated with metabolic abnormalities, such as visceral obesity, dyslipidaemia and insulin resistance, and may precede the development of obesity and T2D. Further, the presence of obesity and T2D increases the risk of fibrosis progression in MASH. Liver disease and mortality related to NAFLD are predicted to continue to rise with the increase in the prevalence of obesity and diabetes, and an ageing population.

The prevalence of NAFLD is higher amongst people with obesity than in the general population and is especially high amongst those with severe obesity (up to 90% according to some estimates).

Around 34% of people with obesity are believed to have MASH. NAFLD and MASH therefore occur in individuals without obesity, and global estimates indicate that 19% of people with NAFLD are lean (BMI&lt;25 kg/m 2  for non-Asians and &lt;23 kg/m 2  for Asians).

Amongst people with T2D, global data indicate that around 66% have MASH, with 41% having significant liver fibrosis.

NAFLD and MASH are multifactorial diseases. Contributing factors include dysregulation of the lipogenic pathway, oxidative stress, genetic predisposition, altered immune responses, and gut microbiome dysbiosis. There is a growing body of evidence linking NAFLD and MASH pathogenesis with

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

mechanisms of metabolic dysfunction, through liver lipid accumulation, insulin resistance, inflammation, apoptosis, and liver fibrosis.

The pathological features of MASH include steatosis, hepatocyte injury, inflammation, and varying degrees of fibrosis. Hepatocyte lipotoxicity and immune-mediated inflammation both play key roles in the pathogenesis of MASH. Hepatic steatosis is associated with lipotoxicity and cellular stresses such as oxidative stress and endoplasmic reticulum stress, which result in hepatocyte injury and apoptosis. Injured hepatocytes and activated Kupffer cells are thought to release proinflammatory cytokines and chemokines that trigger inflammation and fibrosis.

Clinical symptoms of MASH can be absent, and some such as abdominal pain or fatigue are not entirely specific to MASH and can also be difficult to quantify outside of validated questionnaires. Thus, MASH remains underdiagnosed, and people with MASH often present with advanced fibrosis or cirrhosis late in their disease course. Accordingly, there is a marked need for early diagnosis of MASH to manage the disease and the associated complications and avoid the diagnostic inertia that contributes to the substantial clinical and economic burdens of MASH.

Liver biopsies are sufficiently validated to assess the presence of MASH; however, the procedure is invasive and burdensome, contributing to diagnostic inertia. In alignment with current regulatory guidance, liver biopsies are, however, applied in clinical trials, including in the assessment of the degree of liver fibrosis and MASH disease activity. Histological evidence of fibrosis is classified from F0 (no fibrosis) to F4 (cirrhosis) on the MASH CRN fibrosis scale based on pathologist evaluation of a liver biopsy. The fibrosis progression rate in MASH is estimated at 7 years per stage of fibrosis.

MASH is a serious progressive disease with substantial clinical, humanistic, and economic burdens. Still, with liver fibrosis being reversible, the evolution of MASH can be bidirectional, and the progression of MASH could potentially be stabilised or even reversed. However, pharmacotherapeutic options for MASH are sparse and an urgent unmet need for development of novel therapies remains.

Excess body weight is an important risk factor for the development of MASH and progression of liver fibrosis. Although patients may achieve weight loss through lifestyle intervention, many are unable to maintain their weight loss. Global clinical practise guidelines recommend that clinicians consider pharmacotherapy for weight management (with a preference for GLP-1 RAs such as semaglutide 2.4 mg ) as adjunctive therapy to lifestyle modification for individuals with obesity and NAFLD or MASH to promote cardiometabolic health and treat or prevent T2D, cardiovascular disease, and other end-stage manifestations of obesity.

## 2.2. Aspects of development

The application for semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg (hereafter 'semaglutide 2.4 mg') once-weekly for MASH includes data from four clinical studies in the MASH development programme. Table 4 provides an overview. The present application is based on an interim evaluation of the pivotal trial 4553 at week 72, i.e., on data from part 1 of trial 4553. Data from a pivotal dose-finding phase 2 trial (trial 4296) and two supportive trials (trials 4381 and 4492) also contribute to the application.

Non-clinical and clinical information from previous clinical development programmes for semaglutide for the treatment of T2D (project ID NN9535; Ozempic ® ) and for weight management (project ID NN9536; Wegovy ® ) also support the present application.

Data from the cardiovascular outcomes trial (CVOT) SELECT (trial ID EX9536-4388) conducted by the applicant are included to confirm a beneficial effect of semaglutide 2.4 mg on cardiovascular risk in people at risk of MASH. Study EX9536-4388 demonstrated that Wegovy ®  reduces the risk of major adverse cardiovascular events (MACE; a composite outcome comprising cardiovascular death, non-fatal

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

myocardial infarction, or non-fatal stroke) in adults with established cardiovascular disease and either obesity or overweight 46 .

Population pharmacokinetic (PK) analysis was made based on phase 2 and phase 3 data in patients with MASH and F1 to F4 with regards to age, gender, race, and ethnicity.

There are limited data from the use of semaglutide for MASH in pregnant women.

cut-off date (05 September 2024), 1197 subjects had been randomised. The present application is based on an evaluation of data from the first 800 randomised subjects with respect to efficacy-related analyses and on data from all exposed subjects (1195 subjects) by the data cut-off date with respect to safety-related evaluations.

## 2.3. Description of the product

Semaglutide is a glucagon-like peptide-1 (GLP-1) analogue with 94% homology to human GLP-1. It is classified as a GLP-1 receptor agonist (RA). To prolong its half-life to approximately 1 week by slowing the degradation of semaglutide in circulation and decrease its renal clearance, a fatty acid moiety is attached to the peptide backbone of semaglutide. In addition, structural modifications to the backbone have been introduced to increase stability against the DPP-4-mediated degradation and to increase binding of semaglutide to albumin.

Substantial clinical experience with semaglutide for weight management and for the treatment of type 2 diabetes (T2D) are available. Semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg once weekly (Wegovy ® ) is approved for weight management in several countries and regions. In the US, Canada and other places, Wegovy ®  is also approved for cardiovascular risk reduction. Once-weekly semaglutide s.c. (at dose levels 0.5, 1.0 and 2.0 mg) is approved for the treatment of T2D (Ozempic ® ) and, in the US, also for cardiovascular risk reduction in people with T2D and established cardiovascular disease. Oral semaglutide once daily is approved for the treatment of T2D (Rybelsus ® ).

The effects of semaglutide in the body are mediated via specific activation of the GLP-1 receptor and are generally well characterised. Both native GLP-1 and GLP-1 RAs reduce body weight by lowering energy intake via inducing feelings of satiety and fullness and lowering feelings of hunger. Trials with semaglutide have shown reduced energy intake during an ad libitum meal, improved control of eating, less food cravings (for dairy and savoury foods), less desire for sweet food and less preference for high fat food compared to placebo. The mechanism of decreased energy intake is well-studied and involves GLP-1 receptors expressed in the pancreas and the brain in regions that regulates satiety and appetite. Semaglutide lowers blood glucose by a mechanism that increases insulin secretion and reduces glucagon secretion, both depending on the level of glucose in blood.

GLP-1 receptors are also expressed in the heart, blood vessels, as well as on kidney cells and cells of the immune system. However, the GLP-1 receptor has not been detected on liver cells.

## 3. Quality aspects

## 3.1. Introduction

The finished product (FP) is presented as Kayshild, solution for injection in pre-filled pen (0.25 mg, 0.5 mg, 1 mg, 1.7 mg, 2.4 mg) containing 0.68 mg/mL, 1.34 mg/mL, 2.27 mg/mL and 3.2 mg/mL of Semaglutide as active substance (AS). Other ingredients are: Disodium phosphate dihydrate, Propylene glycerol, Phenol, Hydrochloric acid (for pH adjustment), Sodium hydroxide (for pH adjustment) and water for injections.

The product is available in 1.5 mL or 3 mL glass cartridge (type I glass) closed at the one end with a rubber plunger (chlorobutyl) and at the other end with an aluminium cap with a laminated rubber sheet (bromobutyl/polyisoprene) inserted. The cartridge is assembled into a disposable pre-filled multidose PDS290 pen made of polypropylene, polyoxymethylene, polycarbonate and acrylonitrile butadiene styrene. For the pre-filled pen, FlexTouch (0.25, 0.5, 1, 1.7 and 2.4 mg), a pack size of 1 pre-filled pen and 4 disposable NovoFine Plus needles is available.

Semaglutide, the active substance contained in Kayshild, is a glucagon-like peptide-1 (GLP-1) analogue substituted with a linker and a fatty acid side chain. It is produced using recombinant DNA technology in Saccharomyces cerevisiae followed by chemical modifications. Semaglutide is the same active substance contained in the currently authorised products Ozempic and Wegovy.

The Kayshild dossier includes a full Module 3 quality documentation. As this is a new application, all the data has been assessed accordingly.

## 3.2. Active substance

The information on semaglutide as described in Module 3.2.S. of this marketing authorisation application (MAA) is identical to Module 3.2.S of the Ozempic and Wegovy dossiers.

## 3.2.1. General information

The active substance of Kayshild is semaglutide. Semaglutide (INN) is a long-acting analogue of human glucagon like-1 peptide i.e. an Aib 8 , Arg 34 -GLP-1(7-37) analogue substituted on the ε -amino group of the lysine residue in position 26 with an (S)-22,40-dicarboxy-10,19,24-trioxo-3,6,12,15tetraoxa-9,18,23- triazatetracontan-1-oyl side chain. The side chain consists of two 8-amino-3,6dioxaoctanoic acid (ADO) spacers, one γ -glutamic acid (Glu) spacer, and a fatty diacid (1,18octadecanedioic acid). Semaglutide is produced using recombinant DNA technology in yeast (Saccharomyces cerevisiae) and chemical modification.

The structural formula of semaglutide is given in Figure 1.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

\"HI LEO00DSD

CH, CH3

## Figure 1: The Chemical structure of semaglutide

NH

<!-- image -->

Semaglutide acts as a GLP-1 receptor agonist that selectively binds to and activates the GLP-1 receptor, the target for native GLP-1. Compared to native GLP-1, semaglutide has a prolonged half-life of around 1 week making it suitable for once-weekly subcutaneous administration. The principal mechanism of protraction is albumin binding, which results in decreased renal clearance and protection from metabolic degradation. Furthermore, semaglutide is stabilised against degradation by the dipeptidyl peptidase 4 (DPP-4) enzyme. Semaglutide reduces blood glucose through a mechanism where it stimulates insulin secretion and lowers glucagon secretion, both in a glucose-dependent manner.

## Reference to a current marketing authorisation, already held by Novo Nordisk, with the semaglutide active substance

Kayshild is very similar to multiple other authorised products of the applicant Novo Nordisk, namely Rybelsus (EMEA/H/C/004953) Ozempic (EMEA/H/C/004174) and Wegovy (EMEA/H/C/005422). Full module 3 quality documentation is included in the Kayshild dossier. The Applicant states that the module 3 documentation for semaglutide AS is identical to the already authorised products Ozempic and Wegovy. The manufacturing process of semaglutide AS for Rybelsus is slightly different to accommodate further processing into tablets for oral use. Nevertheless, as this concerns a new application, full information for the AS is provided and assessed accordingly. Satisfactory evidence of GMP compliance has been provided.

Following EMA approval of Ozempic and Wegovy, multiple variations have introduced changes to their dossiers. With respect to the active substance semaglutide, the most notable change to the module 3 documentation is the change from manufacturing process A to manufacturing process B, which resulted in a new yeast strain for production and a modified fermentation and recovery process. This change is approved for Wegovy under EMEA/H/C/005422/X/0016 and Ozempic under EMEA/H/C/004174/X/0043.

## 3.2.2. Manufacture, characterisation, and process controls

## Manufacturing process

Semaglutide bulk active substance manufacturing is done at the Novo Nordisk A/S site in Kalundborg, Hallas Alle 1, DK-4400, Denmark. The sites listed here are already authorised for the manufacture and control of semaglutide bulk AS for Ozempic and Wegovy.

Semaglutide is manufactured in yeast ( Saccharomyces cerevisiae ) by expression of an extended semaglutide precursor polypeptide, which is subsequently cleaved enzymatically by enterokinase into the semaglutide precursor and chemically modified to form the final semaglutide molecule. The active

ILE-FATA-W-LZV-R-G-R-G-OM

Lys 2

NH

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

substance manufacturing process is split into fermentation, recovery, purification, modification and acylating agent synthesis parts, with the distinct steps described in flow diagrams, including the operational parameters and in-process tests. Critical in-process controls are marked. The description of the manufacturing process, process parameters and in-process tests is clear and adequate.

The intermediates and the final active substance are isolated and have defined storage containers, conditions and shelf life (24 months at -20 °C). The final active substance is freeze dried and stored 20 °C for up to 48 months. Overall, the description of the manufacturing process is considered acceptable.

## Control of raw materials

Detailed descriptions of the raw materials used during the manufacturing of semaglutide Active substance are provided, with emphasis on the cell substrate, cell bank system, API starting materials (including materials for synthesis of the acylating agent). The construction of the expression plasmid and the source and history of S. cerevisiae strain producing the extended semaglutide precursor is described in detail. The cell banking system of master cell bank (MCB) and working cell bank (WCB) is explained and characterisation of MCB and WCB is reported. Stability results of MCB and WCB are available and raise no concerns.

No animal (or human) derived materials are used in the manufacturing of semaglutide.

The selection of starting materials is identical to that of the already approved product Wegovy.

## Controls of Critical Steps and Intermediates

The critical in-process controls (the combination of critical operational parameters and critical inprocess test) for the manufacturing process of semaglutide active substance (fermentation, recovery and purification) and the synthesis of the acylating agent are described. Critical in-process controls for fermentation, recovery and purification were selected through process justification studies in laboratory scale. For the acylating agent specification, limits are mainly based on the classification and fate of the impurities in this intermediate. The control strategy for the acylating agent is considered appropriate to ensure the quality of the material. Overall, the proposed critical in-process controls and their limits are described in sufficient details, are well justified and considered acceptable.

## Process validation

The evaluation and validation of the semaglutide active substance manufacturing process (process B) is described. The fermentation and recovery processes were previously adopted from the approved Rybelsus product, which was validated in 2017, and validation of this part of the process was not repeated for Kayshild. Process validation for the purification part of the process was based on three consecutive batches for each step.

Laboratory scale process justification studies were used to establish and confirm the ranges for the (critical) in-process controls (parameters and testing) for the semaglutide process B and subsequently design the setup and acceptance criteria for process validation studies. The process validation acceptance criteria were based on a combination of the critical and non-critical operational parameters, critical in-process tests, additional testing (selected non-critical in-process tests to show consistent product quality) and specification tests on semaglutide active substance.

All the results of the fermentation, recovery, purification and final active substance batches met the set acceptance criteria. The removal of product and process related impurities was investigated during the validation of the purification part of the process. The levels of a large number of impurities were monitored over the course of the purification steps and the process was consistently capable of clearing those impurities to acceptable levels.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Additional process validation studies were performed to support changes introduced to the initial manufacturing process, appropriately validating the impacted parts of the process. The collection of reported process validation studies indicate that semaglutide can be consistently manufactured with acceptable quality and purity according to the established process B. The proposed commercial manufacturing process for active substance for Kayshild is considered validated.

## Manufacturing process development

Semaglutide active substance was originally developed as the product of a synthetic manufacturing process. and semaglutide from this synthetic process was used for early phase 1 and phase 2 clinical trials. For clinical phase 3, the manufacturing process was transformed into a recombinant version of the process (process A), which was approved and initially commercialised for Ozempic and later for Wegovy. Recently, Process A was replaced with Process. This change involved the introduction of a different yeast strain which expresses an extended semaglutide precursor polypeptide, requiring the addition of the enterokinase cleavage step and an updated downstream purification process in the manufacture of subcutaneous semaglutide. Comparability between the pre- and post-change products has been demonstrated at the time. The AS manufacturing process now intended for the commercialisation of Kayshild is in accordance with the AS manufacturing process approved for Ozempic and Wegovy.

A clear overview of the differences of each of the iterations of the synthetic and recombinant versions of the semaglutide manufacturing process are provided including which version of the manufacturing process is used for which clinical trial, and which studies showed comparability of this version of the process and the process intended for market. Identical process development steps have been made for the authorised products Ozempic and Wegovy and the comparability assessments of the MAH have been approved for these products

Multiple comparability studies were performed to support the changes to the manufacturing process during development. Most notably, the comparability study between active substance batches manufactured with process A (used for clinical phase 3 trials) and the current manufacturing process B (intended for commercialisation) assessed aspects such as release specifications (and their historical ranges), stability trends, impurity and degradation profiles and verification and characterisation of structural and physico-chemical properties.

Overall, the changes made to the active substance manufacturing process during development have not negatively impacted the quality, safety, or efficacy of the product.

## Characterisation

Data is presented from studies that characterised the structural and physico-chemical properties of semaglutide and the product related impurities that arise during the manufacturing process of the molecule and acylating agent.

The characterisation of the molecule was sufficiently thorough, confirming the semaglutide (primary) structure and determining the physico-chemical characteristics (appearance, solubility, pH in water, charge heterogeneity (pI), UV absorbance and water absorption) and properties (hydrophobicity, hydrodynamic radius).

Extra emphasis was put on the characterisation of the biological activity in relation to the content of semaglutide in active substance and finished product, as determined by RP-HPLC. In general, the specific bioactivity of semaglutide in active substance and finished product was shown to be very stable. A strong correlation was visible between the main peak content and the specific bioactivity of semaglutide, regardless of the purity of the sample. The main peak content determination with the RPHPLC method offers a reliable measure of the bioactivity of semaglutide in both AS and FP.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Thorough investigations were performed into the fate of potential product related impurities in semaglutide active substance, evaluating their clearance during the different steps in the manufacturing process. This allowed the development of control strategies to ensure the quality of the manufactured active substance. Overall, the identification and characterisation of impurities presented is considered adequate.

The results from forced degradation studies show that semaglutide active substance and finished product are susceptible to degradation under most stress conditions (acidic and basic pH, heat, light, reduction and oxidation) but is resistant to mechanical stress.

The suitability of the RP-HPLC method to determine the levels of degradation products of semaglutide subjected to stress conditions was investigated. The specificity of the method was shown by confirming that placebo samples that were exposed to stress conditions did not generate peaks that interfered with semaglutide or semaglutide degradation product peaks. Additionally, evaluation of the mass balance of degraded samples showed that the RP-HPLC method is capable of detecting the majority of the degradation products of semaglutide subjected to extreme conditions. In summary, the RP-HPLC method is suitable for its intended purpose.

Similarly, the SE-HPLC method was shown to be suitable for the determination of the HMWP degradation products, which were found to be a major degradation product of light exposure/stress.

Taken together, the applicant has performed sufficiently thorough characterisation studies into the structure, physical/chemical properties and bioactivity of semaglutide, as well as the formation of degradation products when the molecule is exposed to stress conditions. The information gathered in these studies was used for the design of control strategies for semaglutide quality.

## 3.2.3. Specification

## Specifications

The active substance specification is presented and includes tests for appearance, identity, content, hydrophilic impurities, hydrophobic impurities, sum of impurities, high molecular weight proteins, specific bioactivity, bacterial endotoxins, Total Aerobic Microbial Count, loss of drying and host cell proteins.

The control strategy for semaglutide active substance was developed, largely based on the identified critical quality attributes. For those attributes where a need was identified to control them at active substance release, specifications were set based on an approach focused on process capability (Cpk) calculations. Over 300 batches were used for setting specifications, including batches used for clinical phase 3 trials, commercial production for Process A and Process B and including PV batches. The presented specifications are identical to those of the already approved product Wegovy and are considered justified and acceptable.

A number of items are not controlled by the active substance specification, mostly process related impurities. This is justified by their highly effective removal during the manufacturing process of semaglutide. Residual DNA levels for process B batches were consistently below the WHO guideline limits. Similarly, the residual enterokinase levels were consistently below the limit of quantification of the analytical method. Therefore, the exclusion of these process related impurities from the specification is considered acceptable.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Analytical procedures and reference standards

The non-pharmacopeial analytical procedures from the active substance specification are provided. The controls to assess method performance are generally acceptable. For the Host Cell Protein determination, additional information is provided regarding the coverage of the antibody reagents used in this method, which is considered acceptable.

Compendial methods have been verified to be suitable for semaglutide active substance, and noncompendial methods have been validated according to ICH guidelines. Dilutional linearity was included as a validation parameter of the Host Cell Proteins method. Clear validation summaries of the noncompendial methods are provided. Taken together, the validation data presented for the analytical procedures of semaglutide active substance show that they are suitable for their intended purpose.

A two-tiered reference standard system is in place for Kayshild, consisting of a semaglutide primary reference material (PRM) and a semaglutide secondary reference material (SRM). The same reference materials are used for the approved semaglutide products Ozempic and Wegovy.

Extensive characterisation testing results are shown for the PRM. Because there is a well-defined correlation between content and bioactivity, the semaglutide unit for bioactivity is defined as one unit (U) is equal to one milligram of semaglutide. The content of semaglutide in the PRM batch is assigned by determining the nitrogen content (total protein content) and correcting this with the sum of impurities determined with RP-HPLC. This approach was used to calibrate and assign the content (with RP-HPLC) and specific bioactivity of the semaglutide SRM batches which are in turn used for the determination of the content and specific bioactivity of semaglutide active substance. Additionally, the semaglutide PRMs and SRMs serve as reference materials for identity determination.

Protocols for new reference standard lots are included in the dossier. Overall, the information provided regarding reference standards of semaglutide is considered adequate.

## Batch analysis

Results from batch analyses of batches of semaglutide active substance manufactured according to process B are presented. Additionally, results from batches used during development (manufactured according to process A) are presented. The batches presented have been used in early phase 1 trials, phase 2 trials, clinical pharmacology studies and phase 3 trials and in some cases for clinical trials for other development products. All results complied with the proposed specification limits at the time of release.

Some of the batches have been used to support claims of comparability between batches manufactured for clinical studies and batches manufactured with the proposed commercial process. Results for batches which were manufactured to support the last manufacturing process change for semaglutide and therefore represent the intended commercial process, indicate consistent manufacturing of semaglutide active substance.

## Container closure

Semaglutide active substance is a solid (freeze-dried) substance and stored in containers with screw caps below or at -20 °C. Stability samples are stored in equivalent containers of reduced size. The same storage container was used for storage of semaglutide active substance intended for use in clinical trials. The selection of the container closure system for semaglutide active substance is considered justified.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 3.2.4. Stability

A shelf life of 48 months is claimed for semaglutide active substance when stored at -20 °C ± 5 °C. This claim is based on stability studies at the long-term storage condition and at the accelerated condition (+5 °C ± 3 °C). Active substance batches (three) manufactured with the manufacturing process B are considered the primary stability batches, and three process B PV batches and four process A batches are also included in the stability study. Currently, the stability studies at accelerated conditions are all finalised just like the studies for batches manufactured with process A. Studies at the long-term storage condition for batches manufactured with process B have 36 and 18 months of data reported. The applicant has committed to finalize these ongoing studies.

Stability testing items are acceptable, with a focus on impurities from the RP-HPLC and SE-HPLC methods. For both the long-term storage condition and the accelerated condition, the presented stability study data are within the acceptance criteria and show no changes over time. As process A and process B have been shown to be comparable and have the same storage container and conditions, and 60 months of stability data at the long-term storage condition has been reported for process A, the proposed shelf-lif e of 48 months at -20 °C ± 5 °C for semaglutide active substance is endorsed.

## 3.3. Finished medicinal product

## 3.3.1. Description of the product and pharmaceutical development

## Description of the product

Semaglutide finished products (0.25 mg, 0.5 mg, 1.0 mg, 1.7 mg and 2.4 mg) are solutions for injection and are presented in four different concentrations containing 0.68 mg/ml, 1.34 mg/ml, 2.27 mg/ml and 3.2 mg/ml. The finished product is a colourless or almost colourless liquid free from turbidity and essentially free from particulate matter.

- Semaglutide 0.68 mg/mL is filled in a 1.5 ml cartridge and in a 3 ml cartridge (Semaglutide doses 0.25 and 0.5 mg both contain 0.68 mg in one mL but have different injectable volumes).
- Semaglutide 1.34 mg/mL, semaglutide 2.27 mg/ml and semaglutide 3.2 mg/ml are filled in a 3 ml cartridge

All finished products are assembled in a PDS290 pen-injector for semaglutide.

The composition of semaglutide 0.68 mg/ml, semaglutide 1.34 mg/ml, semaglutide 2.27 mg/ml and semaglutide 3.2 mg/ml is identical except for the content of the active pharmaceutical ingredient.

All excipients are well known pharmaceutical ingredients and their quality is compliant with Ph. Eur standards. There are no novel excipients used in the finished product formulation.

The primary container closure system of Kayshild Finished Product is a cartridge of either 1.5 mL or 3 mL. The cartridges are made of glass and are closed at one end with a cap with a (non-natural) rubber disc and at the other end with a rubber plunger. The cartridges are assembled in a PDS290 Peninjector.

## Reference to a current marketing authorisation, already hold by Novo Nordisk, with the semaglutide active substance

Kayshild is very similar to multiple other authorised products of the applicant Novo Nordisk, namely Ozempic (EMEA/H/C/004174) and Wegovy (EMEA/H/C/005422). Full module 3 quality documentation

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

for Semaglutide (the active substance of Kayshild), is included in the Kayshild dossier.

Kayshild is presented as a finished product in five distinct strengths filled in a multi-dose (PDS290) pen-injector. This is highly comparable with the approved product Wegovy, which offers the same strengths and an identical multi-dose PDS290 pen-injector. It should be noted that Wegovy offers two presentations for the delivery of 0.5 mg doses, i.e. 1.34 mg/mL, 1.5 mL cartridge and 0.68 mg/mL, 3 mL cartridge, whereas Kayshild 0.5 mg will only be available in the 0.68 mg/mL, 3 mL cartridge presentation. The main differences between the Kayshild and Wegovy submissions are related to streamlining of the documents that were submitted for Wegovy through variations and the exclusion of the 1.34 mg/mL, 1.5 mL cartridge multi-dose and the single dose pre-filled pen presentations of Wegovy.

## Pharmaceutical development

The Kayshild finished products in a PDS290 pen-injector are developed based on the Quality Target Product Profile (QTPP) adopted from Wegovy. The semaglutide finished products intended for market are identical to the products approved as Wegovy and there are no differences in the physical, chemical and overall quality attributes compared to Wegovy.

The compositions of the finished products used during clinical trials and intended for market are described. All the multidose formulations intended for market were tested in the phase 3 clinical trial and these formulations are identical to those approved for Wegovy.

Single use prefilled syringes were also used for Phase 3 clinical trials (but are not intended for market). The used device is identical to the Wegovy single dose pen-injector system, and bio-equivalence with the multidose pen-injector has been appropriately demonstrated.

The development of the manufacturing process of Kayshild Finished Product for manufacturing of batches for Phase 1 and 2, Phase 3 and intended for market is described. The manufacturing process is identical to the process of Wegovy and has remained essentially the same from the manufacture of finished products for the clinical trials to the manufacturing process intended for the market. Comparability of the finished product used in clinical development and intended for market is demonstrated through the primary stability data and the process validation data of processes intended for market.

Extractable and leachable studies have been performed with the cartridge components and raised no concerns. The primary container closure system and PDS-290 pen injector were shown to be fully compatible with the Kayshild Finished Product.

## Manufacture

The applicant provides an overview of all the sites involved in the manufacturing of Kayshild finished product. Formulation, filling and quality control of finished product cartridges is performed at the Novo Nordisk sites in Denmark (Bagsvaerd and Hilleroed) and at the Novo Nordisk site in Clayton, United States. Assembly, packaging and quality control of finished product is performed at the Novo Nordisk Site in Chartres, France and at Novo Nordisk Bgsvaerd, Denmark. The manufacturing responsibilities of sites for Kayshild are identical to those sites involved in Wegovy finished product manufacturing and control. Satisfactory evidence of GMP compliance has been provided for all sites involved in the manufacturing, testing and batch release of the finished product.

The manufacturing process for Kayshild finished product is described through flow diagrams which include the process controls. The manufacturing process is identical to the process of Wegovy.

Following sterilizing filtration the product is filled aseptically into depyrogenated and sterilised cartridges. Closed cartridges are inserted into assembled pen-injectors forming the final finished

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

product. Non-critical process parameters for each manufacturing site and batch size as well as the manufacturing steps and process controls for the Pen-Injector are clearly presented in a separate document. The process time from the end of formulation to the end of filling of the sterile filtered final solution is described and is limited by the media fill validation for the specific site and batch size. Overall, the description of the manufacturing process and parameters is adequate.

The manufacturing process for the PDS290 Pen-injector for Kayshild is described clearly with a flow diagram showing the pre-assembly and final assembly steps. Additionally, exploded views of the parts of the spring and motor modules (that are pre-assembled) and their final assembly are shown.

## Process controls

The controls of critical steps and intermediates of the finished product manufacturing process for Kayshild are described, including the actions when the limits are exceeded. Critical steps were identified through risk assessments (see also 3.2.P.3.5) and limits were set during process justification studies. The pH of the formulated solution and the temperature of the final solution were identified as critical and in-process controls and accompanying limits were set as described in this section. More general critical in-process controls include the bioburden before sterile filtration, the container closure integrity and extractable volume of the cartridges and the inspection for visible foreign particles. Sterilizing filtration is performed after formulation and at filling point and filter integrity testing is performed according to described instructions and limits.

Overall, the proposed critical in-process controls and their limits are described in sufficient detail, are well justified and considered acceptable.

## Process validation / verification

The process validation and verification activities performed by the applicant to support Kayshild finished product manufacturing are a combination of process design, process validation and continued process verification. Kayshild finished product and the corresponding manufacturing process and manufacturing sites are the same as for the approved product Wegovy. The initial process development is based on experience from laboratory scale experiments, pilot/manufacturing scale batches for clinical trials, manufacturing scale batches for process design, process validation studies and continued process verification. Findings from the process design activities are described in process justification reports which also include the risk assessments that are the basis of the design of the critical process controls. The information provided by the applicant related to process design for Kayshild finished product is acceptable.

Initially the finished product (formulation and filling) manufacturing process was validated at the Bagsvaerd site and subsequently the Hilleroed and Clayton sites were added. The validation design and acceptance criteria are generally aligned between those sites, and a bracket design was applied including the lowest and highest semaglutide concentrations. The acceptance criteria for each site include the In-process controls, extensive sampling and non-critical process parameters. The process time from end of formulation sterile filtration to end of filling was included in the validation and at any time limited by the performed media fill validation for the specific process and the specific site. Sterile filter validation is described and the operational parameters for sterile filtration and filter integrity testing are supported. Validation of the assembly process of the PDS290 pen-injector included the appearance, injection time and activation force parameters that are in place as critical in-process controls. The process validation summary reports and the results contained in them raise no concerns and the established manufacturing process is capable of consistently and reproducibly producing Kayshild finished product.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 3.3.2. Product specification

## Specifications

A finished product specification is presented for each of the different concentrations and cartridge volumes of the finished product of Kayshild (0.68 mg/mL - 3.2 mg/mL, 1.5 mL and 3 mL cartridge). The specifications include appearance, identity, content, pH, high molecular weight proteins, impurities, bacterial endotoxins, sterility, identity and content of preservative, particulate matter, dose accuracy, and extractable volume.

The Kayshild finished products intended for market are identical to the products approved as Wegovy and there are no differences in the physical, chemical and overall quality attributes compared to Wegovy. Therefore, the control strategy and specification limits for Kayshild finished product are identical to those for Wegovy. A risk-based approach was used to establish the control strategy and to identify manufacturing process parameters that have an impact on the CQAs. The specifications and inprocess controls for critical steps were based on this.

Specification limits are justified from a safety perspective. The levels of impurities in finished Product (HWMP, Hydrophilic and Hydrophobic impurities) used in non-clinical studies were always higher than the acceptance criteria during the entire finished product shelf-life. As the acceptance criteria for Kayshild finished Product are identical to the acceptance criteria of the approved product Wegovy, they are also considered clinically justified.

The proposed specifications are considered justified and the design of the finished product control strategy for Kayshild is considered acceptable.

## Analytical procedures and reference standards

The non-pharmacopeial analytical procedures from the finished product specification are provided. For other methods, compliance to Ph. Eur. is claimed or ISO guidelines (Dose Accuracy) are referenced. The controls to assess method performance are generally acceptable. Only minimal changes were introduced going from procedures used during clinical trials and procedures to be used for Kayshild intended for the market.

Compendial methods have been verified to be suitable for Kayshild finished product and noncompendial methods have been validated according to ICH Q2 (R1) guideline. Clear validation summaries of the non-compendial methods are provided. The dose accuracy method (which is based on ISO-11608) was verified for suitability of testing the PDS290 Pen-injector for semaglutide finished products. Taken together, the validation data presented for the analytical procedures of Kayshild finished product show they are suitable for their intended purpose.

Reference Standards are described in the Active Substance Section.

## Batch analysis

Batch release data for Kayshild finished product are provided supporting process validation, clinical trials and comparability. An overview of batch analysis results comparing multiple batches from the different commercial manufacturing sites shows that Kayshild finished product can be consistently manufactured with comparable quality.

## Characterisation of impurities

For Kayshild finished product, risk assessments for elemental impurities and nitrosamine impurities were performed according to the appropriate guidance. Based on worst case calculations, none of the elemental impurities exceeded the 30% control threshold of ICH Q3D. The nitrosamine risk assessment (which takes into consideration semaglutide active substance, excipients, primary packaging materials and the finished product) concluded a negligible risk. The conclusions from the risk assessments for

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

elemental impurities and nitrosamine impurities are endorsed.

The characterisation of impurities in Kayshild finished product is described. The manufacturing of finished product introduces no impurities that were not present in the semaglutide active substance. During storage of the finished product, the formation of degradation products is visible. The impurities formed after storage at accelerated conditions were characterised to confirm their identity. No new impurities were found in degraded finished product batches, and the batches representative of the clinical trials had the same degradation products as the batches representative of the commercial process. The characterisation of Kayshild finished product impurities was sufficiently thorough and raises no concerns.

## Container closure

The primary container closure system of Kayshild finished product is a cartridge of either 1.5 mL or 3 mL. The cartridges are identical to those used for Wegovy presentations of the PDS290 pen-injector and are made of chemically inert colourless glass as defined as Type I in Ph. Eur. 3.2.1. The cartridges are siliconized prior to depyrogenation and the silicon used for this was assessed in extractable studies. The cartridges are closed at the one end with a cap with a double layered laminated (non-natural) rubber disc. The layer that is in contact with the finished product is made of bromobutyl rubber. At the other end, a chlorobutyl rubber plunger closes the cartridge. The plunger is siliconized prior to sterilisation. Both the cap and the plunger meet the Ph. Eur. requirements for type I rubber. The description of the materials primary container closure system components is adequate.

The PDS290 multi-dose pen injector for Kayshild is already approved for use and commercialised by the applicant for other products, such as Wegovy. The PDS290 pen-injector for semaglutide variants can deliver 4 doses of 0.25 mg, 0.5 mg, 1 mg, 1.7 mg or 2.4 mg of semaglutide per cartridge, in a volume of 370 μ L or 750 μ L. Compliance of the pen injector with ISO 13485 and ISO 11608-1:2014 is stated.

A detailed summary of the features of the different PDS290 pen-injectors indicate that the design, user interface, intended use and use environments of the Kayshild pen-injector overlap within the PDS290 family. This is leveraged to justify the bridging of studies on biological evaluation, human factors engineering and design verification. Technical information is provided detailing the operation principles of the PDS290 Pen injector and its key functional and additional features. The information provided is sufficient and raises no concerns.

The verification of the functional performance of the design of the PDS290 pen-injector for semaglutide is described. Testing of deliverable volume, dose accuracy, activation force, injection time and visual inspection were included. Based on the results reported it can be concluded that under a range of expected and extreme conditions, the PDS290 pen-injector for Kayshild functions adequately. The dose accuracy, injection time and activation force have been implemented in the control strategy for Kayshild finished product as specifications and in-process control testing providing an extra level of control of the quality of the PDS290 pen-injector.

The compatibility between the NovoFine plus needles (which are co-packaged with the PDS290 pen injector for Kayshild) and the PDS290 pen-injector was shown.

The applicant has performed various risk assessments according to ISO standards to identify and evaluate hazards and hazardous situations of the use of the PDS290 pen-injector. All identified risks have been reduced as far as reasonably possible. Reference is made to a human factors engineering and usability study report included in the submission. From the risk assessments and usability studies it can be concluded that the PDS290 finished products are safe and effective for the intended use.

A Declaration of Conformity (TÜV SÜD) is provided in the dossier. A notified body opinion confirming

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

compliance of the PDS290 pen-injector with the relevant safety and performance requirements according to Article 117, Regulation (EU) 2017/745 on Medical Devices is provided in the dossier.

## 3.3.3. Stability of the product

A description of the stability programme for Kayshild finished product is presented along with a summary of the purpose of each study, the batches included and their batch volume, storage conditions and the status at the time of the submission. The following studies are included:

- Primary stability studies
- Stability studies on PV batches from site Bagsvaerd, Hilleroe and Clayton
- Stability in device
- Stability testing of device functional parameters
- Stability studies on semaglutide manufactured using active substance process B
- In-use stability
- Photo stability

Studies were performed according to applicable ICH guidelines where relevant. For Kayshild finished product, the applicant proposes a 36 months shelf life at 5 °C ± 3 °C for finished product assembled in the PDS290 pen-injector, with an in-use period of 42 days (6 weeks) below 30 °C. The applicant indicates that no changes in formulation or in the materials that are in contact with the finished product were introduced between the primary stability batches and the batches of finished product manufactured with active substance from process B (intended for market). The stability studies were either performed in the primary containers (1.5 mL or 3 mL cartridge) or primary containers assembled into the PDS290 pen-injectors. The design of the described stability studies for Kayshild finished product is acceptable.

At the longterm storage condition (5 °C ± 3 °C), primary stability batches show some upward trends in the impurity levels over the course of 36 months, while content of semaglutide remains stable. However, all results remain within the shelf-life acceptance criteria for long term-storage, over all the 16 primary stability batches. No changes are observed for attributes. Stability studies at the long termstorage condition for batches from Process Validation, batches assembled in the PDS-290 pen injector and batches manufactured with active substance material from Process B are not all finalised yet but follow the same trends.

When the primary stability batches are stored at accelerated stability conditions (25 °C ± 2 °C), similar trends are visible compared to the long-term storage condition. Trends in impurities are more pronounced, as expected. A slight decrease in semaglutide content is visible. Batches from Process Validation, batches assembled in the PDS-290 pen injector and batches manufactured with active substance material from Process B follow the same trends.

A Stability study of the PDS290 pen-injector functional parameters (Dose Accuracy, Injection time, Activation force) support the proposed shelf life of 36 months at 5 °C ± 3 °C.

The proposed in-use period for Kayshild is 42 days below 30 °C and the in-use stability studies on primary batches support this. This includes in-use simulation close to manufacturing date, mid-shelf life and near the end of shelf life. The efficacy of the preservative phenol is maintained during the inuse period, in line with the requirements in Ph. Eur. Dose accuracy of the pen-injector was confirmed at the end of the in-use period.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Photostability studies in line with ICH guidelines showed that finished product in PDS290 Pen-injector with the cap on is stable when exposed to light, indicating that the device provides adequate protection from product degradation. Without the cap, the finished product shows increased degradation. In line with the findings in the photostability studies, instructions regarding the pen cap are found in the SmPC: 'Keep the pen cap on when the pen is not in use in order to protect it from light'.

Finally, the applicant reports that freezing of Kayshild finished products poses a risk for the sterility of the product and should therefore be avoided. Appropriate instructions are included in the SmPC: 'Store in a refrigerator (2 °C-8 °C). Keep away from the cooling element. Do not freeze'.

Based on the data presented in the Kayshild finished product stability studies, the applicant proposes a 36 months (3 years) shelf-life for finished product assembled in the PDS290 peninjector at 5 °C ± 3 °C. This is endorsed. The proposed shelf life and in-use period are correctly reflected by the SmPC.

## 3.3.4. Post approval change management protocols

A set of Post-Approval Change Management Protocols is included in this submission. All of the PACMPs presented for semaglutide active substance for Kayshild or for Kayshild finished product have been previously approved for Wegovy and in some cases the Type IB variation for the specific change detailed in the protocols has also been approved.

## PACMP for equipment at the site Kalundborg

A protocol for the introduction of an additional equipment at the Kalundborg site of Novo Nordisk is described. This protocol is a generic protocol which can be used for the introduction of equipment at this specific site and has been already executed for the introduction of an additional equipment for the manufacturing of semaglutide active substance for Wegovy and is included in the current dossier for Kayshild.

The protocol is written in line with EMA/CHMP/CVMP/QWP/586330/2010, Questions and answers on post approval change management protocol, with clearly described changes, a risk assessment of the proposed change, the design of a comparability study and the reporting category and documents to be submitted. The comparability study proposed contains an assessment of active substance release specification data, comparative characterisation of impurity profiles by HPLC and stability trends at accelerated conditions. The PACMP for an additional equipment at site Kalundborg is acceptable.

## PACMP for Additional Purification Facility - Building KA, Kalundborg, Denmark

A protocol for the introduction of an additional purification facility for semaglutide in Kalundborg is presented. This protocol was approved for Wegovy and no reporting variation has been submitted for Wegovy or for Kayshild.

In the protocol, it is proposed to introduce an additional purification facility for semaglutide active substance at the Kalundborg site. A site-specific technical adaptation will be introduced.

The change is described clearly and is accompanied with a risk assessment of the impact of the described changes. The process validation and comparability studies proposed to support this change are designed based on this risk assessment. The comparability study assesses data from Critical inprocess tests, active substance release tests, HPLC impurity profiles, stability studies at accelerated conditions and additional tests for process related impurities, and the design is endorsed.

The protocol is written in line with EMA/CHMP/CVMP/QWP/586330/2010, Questions and answers on post approval change management protocol and raises no concerns.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## PACMP for Additional Finished Product Manufacturing Sites

A general protocol for the introduction of an additional manufacturing site for the formulation, filling and inspection of bulk semaglutide finished products is presented. The formulation, method of manufacture, filling, container closure system, testing, and specifications at the proposed facility will be the same as that of the currently approved manufacturing site(s). This protocol is highly similar to a protocol approved for Wegovy.

The protocol contains a risk evaluation of adding the additional manufacturing site and a testing plan to demonstrate comparability. Process validation will be performed according to a scenario that depends on which finished product concentrations and/or cartridge volumes will be manufactured at the new site.

Testing to support the change includes validation testing (including extensive sampling to evaluate homogeneity, in-process control testing, release testing (against specifications and for comparability) and stability testing. The validation strategy is in-line with the validation strategy described for Kayshild finished products. This is endorsed. When applicable, analytical test methods for Kayshild finished product quality control will be transferred to the new site without introducing any changes. The protocol is written in line with EMA/CHMP/CVMP/QWP/586330/2010, Questions and answers on post approval change management protocol and raises no concerns.

## 3.3.5. Adventitious agents

The Semaglutide that is used as an active substance in Kayshild is manufactured recombinantly in yeast. Saccharomyces cerevisiae does not support the propagation of mammalian viruses. No raw materials or excipients of human or animal origin are used for the manufacture of semaglutide AS or Kayshild FP. Testing for bacteria, fungi and mycoplasma is performed adequately. The conclusion of the applicant that the finished product is safe with regards to virus, transmissible spongiform encephalopathy agents, bacteria, mycoplasma, and fungi is endorsed.

## 3.3.6. Genetically modified organisms (GMO)

Not applicable.

## 3.4. Discussion and conclusions on chemical, pharmaceutical and biological aspects

Kayshild is a preparation of the GLP-1 agonist semaglutide, suitable for once-weekly subcutaneous injection. Kayshild is very similar to multiple other authorised products of the applicant Novo Nordisk, namely Ozempic (EMEA/H/C/004174) and Wegovy (EMEA/H/C/005422).

The presented information on development, manufacture and control of the semaglutide active substance is satisfactory.

Kayshild is presented as a finished product in five distinct strengths filled in a multi-dose (PDS290) pen-injector. This is highly comparable with the approved product Wegovy, which offers the same strengths and an identical multi-dose PDS290 pen-injector. The presented information on development, manufacture and control of the finished product is satisfactory.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 3.5. Recommendations for future quality development

Not applicable.

## 4. Non-clinical aspects

## 4.1. Introduction

Semaglutide has a 94% structural homology to native GLP-1, a molecular weight of 4113,58 g/mol and is good soluble in an aqueous solution. Semaglutide is suitable for once-weekly administration in humans.

The pharmacological mechanism of GLP-1R agonists is well described in the literature, with blood glucose lowering and body fat loss mediated by lowered intake of calories. The primary pharmacological target tissues for GLP-1R agonists are the pancreas (beta-cells), the gastrointestinal system and the brain. The amino acid sequence of GLP-1 is preserved in mammals and only one receptor, the GLP-1R, has been identified. Rat and human GLP-1R have 90% homology and monkey and human 99%. The GLP-1R is a G-protein coupled receptor and the cellular action of GLP-1 is mediated through the G-protein and subsequent activation of adenylate cyclase leading to increased cAMP accumulation.

Semaglutide is approved in the EU for treatment of type 2 diabetes mellitus and for weight management. Two new non-clinical studies dosing semaglutide 2.4 mg are presented to support the proposed indication:

- DIO-NASH mouse (Diet-Induced Obese Non-Alcoholic SteatoHepatitis, study 321911), Semaglutide efficacy on NASH-relevant parameters in male C57Bl/6 mice fed a DIO-NASH (high fat, -fructose, cholesterol) diet

- CDAA-HFD-NASH mouse (Choline Deficient Amino Acid defined High Fat Diet Non-Alcoholic SteatoHepatitis, study 321945), Effect of semaglutide on NASH-relevant parameters in male C57Bl/6 mice fed a CDAA HFD (choline-deficient, amino acid-defined) diet.

## 4.2. Analytical methods

The methods developed for analysis of semaglutide in plasma with LC-MS/MS (mouse, rat, monkey) and ELISA (mouse, rabbit, monkey) were sufficiently validated with satisfactory assay performance.

The LOCI assay was affected by interference from the plasma matrix and dilution linearity issues with a larger impact on low concentrations leading to underestimation of semaglutide exposures (rat, rabbit, monkey). For this reason, the plasma assay in rat and monkey was replaced by LC-MS/MS and ELISA. In the rabbit embryo-foetal development study (207360), measured concentration were below 200 nM, where Hook effect occurred and the values for dose-normalised average concentrations (Cavg) did not deviate from the other tests.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 4.3. Pharmacology

## 4.3.1. Pharmacodynamics

## 4.3.1.1. Primary pharmacodynamics

In support of the present indication for MASH, two non-clinical studies were conducted to evaluate the biological activity and mechanism of action of semaglutide in the liver: DIO-NASH mouse model (DietInduced Obese Non-Alcoholic SteatoHepatitis) and CDAA-HFD-NASH mouse model (Choline Deficient Amino Acid defined High Fat Diet Non-Alcoholic SteatoHepatitis).

In the DIO-NASH model, NASH-progression is driven by metabolic dysfunction and mice display significantly elevated quantitative markers of liver lipid accumulation, inflammation and liver fibrosis. Semaglutide reduced body weight and liver weight compared to vehicle, and reduced circulating markers of liver injury, reduced inflammation and disease activity as measured by the NAS score. Maximum effects were reached by dosing 123 µg/kg subcutaneously daily for 16-24 weeks. In the liver, semaglutide decreased lipid accumulation. Non-fasted plasma insulin was elevated in the DIO NASH model compared to chow vehicle and semaglutide significantly reduced the glucose excursion in an intraperitoneal glucose tolerance test (ipGTT).

In the CDAA-HFD model, NASH progression is driven by blocked export of very-low density lipoproteins secondary to choline deficiency and mice are lean and show non-metabolic driven increases in hepatomegaly, plasma liver enzymes, steatosis, inflammation and progressive fibrotic development. Semaglutide reduced body weight and liver weight compared to vehicle and reduced circulating markers of liver injury and inflammation. Maximum effects were reached by dosing 20 µg/kg subcutaneously daily for 6-12 weeks. However, semaglutide did not reduce lipid accumulation in the liver, nor did it decrease disease activity. When challenged in an ipGTT, semaglutide treatment did not further affect glucose excursions. Fasting insulin was reduced in animals on CDAA HFD diet compared to chow fed animals. On request it was clarified that it was expected that semaglutide would not reduce hepatic triglyceride levels in the CDAA-HFD mouse model, therefore translatability to humans is not limited. In the CDAA-HFD model, the choline deficiency coupled with lower levels of dietary methionine blocks the export of triglycerides in VLDL particles and severely limits fat oxidation. Consequently, it becomes nearly impossible to dispose of the fat trapped within the liver in this preclinical model. This does however still allow for supporting the MoA understanding: the beneficial effects observed following treatment with semaglutide despite persistent hepatic steatosis suggest that semaglutide does not decrease MASH and hepatic fibrosis solely through reduction of hepatic lipids. To study the effect of semaglutide on hepatic steatosis, the GAN DIO NASH model is a better translational choice of model and, indeed, hepatic lipids are reduced following treatment with semaglutide similar to what is observed in patients.

In the CDAA-HFD model, only terminal blood samples were included. Accordingly, study specific ALT/AST measurement at pre-dose i.e., baseline for the semaglutide and chow reversal group are not available. However, there is no reason to believe that the semaglutide and chow reversal groups should be different at week 6 compared to the baseline group as all groups had been on the same diet and none of the groups had been dosed at this point in the study. Accordingly, it can be assumed that the starting levels of ALT/AST were identical across groups. With that in mind, a reduction in ALT/AST was observed between week 6 and week 12 (the two last timepoints for which ALT/AST data are available) in the vehicle group. If semaglutide had no effect on liver enzymes, the decrease in ALT/AST should follow the same pattern. However, this is not the case: ALT/AST was decreased already after 6 weeks with semaglutide, showing the effect on liver enzymes with treatment. Hereafter, the effect

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

'plateaus out' allowing the vehicle group to 'catch up' and eliminating the possibility to detect an effect of semaglutide at this later timepoint. In support of this interpretation, longitudinal data on ALT and AST have been reported by Matsumoto et al (2013) in the CDAA-HFD model showing that liver enzyme levels peak around six weeks after initiating the CDAA-HFD and then continuously decline during the subsequent 12 weeks.

A scientific discussion about how semaglutide directly and indirectly modulates MASH was provided on request. In MASH, insulin resistance in hepatic and adipose tissues alongside enhances hepatic de novo lipogenesis increases lipolysis in the adipose tissue. The increased lipolysis promotes the accumulation of lipids in the liver and delivers an excessive amount of toxic lipid species which may cause cellular stress and inflammation. Semaglutide treatment improves insulin resistance thereby restoring the metabolic balance in the liver and adipose tissue. Furthermore, though the GLP1 receptor is not expressed in liver, central GLP1R activation by semaglutide decreases circulating levels of TNF α via adrenergic and opioid receptor signalling and attenuates systemic inflammation and contributes to the beneficial effects of semaglutide on liver fibrosis. Given the lack of GLP1 receptor expression in the liver of both humans and mice, the effects on MASH are considered indirect, likely mediated both by the weight-loss per se and by weight-loss-independent mechanisms. The current non-clinical data does not discern weight-loss-dependent from weight-loss-independent effects as weight-matched control groups, i.e. a group in which food intake was reduced to induce a weight loss identical to semaglutide, were not included.

On request it was clarified why no non-rodent species or independent fibrotic model (e.g., carbon tetrachloride, bile duct ligation) was included to confirm reproducibility of antifibrotic activity and to ensure translational validity. The applicant has conducted pharmacology studies in the non-clinical NASH models considered to offer the highest degree of translation to humans. The model selection is supported by the international LITMUS consortium which ranked the GAN DIO-NASH Mouse model among the highest, most translational murine models of NASH. At the time of study conceptualisation, rodent models were more thoroughly characterised in terms of disease progression and, especially, response to pharmacotherapy compared to non-rodent models. Consequently, it was decided not to use non-rodent models. Presently, human data is available to support the effect of semaglutide in patients with MASH and show translation between the applied mouse models and humans. Bridging studies in non-rodent species are not planned to be performed, in accordance with the 3Rs, as they are considered to provide minimal additional value.

Toxin-induced models do not recapitulate the lipo-toxicity which is central to the pathogenesis of NASH. As the GLP-1 receptor is not expressed by the liver and the beneficial effects of semaglutide in MASH are indirect, the applicant considered that the toxin-induced models are of less translational relevance also with regards to fibrosis. In contrast, the lipo-toxicity is reflected in both the GAN DIO NASH model and in the CDAA-HFD model and these, therefore, offer more relevant and translational alternatives to study the effect of semaglutide in MASH. There is no rat model equivalent to the GAN DIO NASH mouse model and the mouse CDAA-HFD model was selected instead of a rat CDAA-HFD model because the mouse model had been much better characterised. This was accepted by the CHMP.

In support of semaglutide for type 2 diabetes mellitus and for weight management data was assessed at the time of marketing authorisation application. The efficacy pharmacodynamic studies using semaglutide have been conducted in vitro , ex vivo as well as in vivo in normal, diabetic and obese rodent models and normal pigs and minipigs. The studies have shown that semaglutide has pharmacological properties consistent with a GLP-1R agonist showing increases of insulin secretion, plasma glucose lowering and weight lowering due to a reduction of food intake. Furthermore, it was confirmed that semaglutide crosses the BBB, and that its effects include central homeostatic mechanisms involving the hypothalamus and brain stem.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 4.3.1.2. Secondary pharmacodynamics

A broad profiling screening panel using 68 biochemical receptors, ion-channels and neurotransmitter transporters did not show a competitive interaction with semaglutide. Also, semaglutide, up to 10 μ M, did not activate the glucagon receptor. No secondary pharmacology effects are expected from semaglutide.

## 4.3.1.3. Safety pharmacology

The safety pharmacology studies were designed to investigate the effect of semaglutide on major organ function (central nervous system, respiratory system and cardiovascular system). Exposure measurements in both the rat CNS study and in the cynomolgus monkey cardiovascular study exposure of treated animals confirmed exposure of treated animals could correlate effects to the exposure. Due to differences in dosing frequency between humans (once weekly) and animals (daily/biweekly), the mean maximal plasma concentration (Cmax) at the maximum recommended human dose (MRHD) of 2.4 mg/week has been used for exposure comparison in the safety pharmacology section.
