## 5.3.10. Overall discussion and conclusions on clinical efficacy

## 5.3.10.1. Discussion

## Dose finding

The dose selection was primarily based on the study results of the dose response phase 2 study 4296 and the experience as derived from previous studies including T2DM and weight management, which have been part of the respective MAAs. An important learning from these previous studies was that a weekly dosing is associated with less GI symptoms than once daily dose. Further, dose escalation has been shown to be associated with less GI symptoms and greater tolerability, which would support the 16 weeks intended dose escalation.

The design of the phase 2 study of a 72-week, multinational, multicentre, randomised, double-blind, six-armed, parallel-group, placebo controlled, multiple-dose trial comparing the efficacy and safety of semaglutide s.c. 0.1 mg, 0.2 mg and 0.4 mg once daily (OD) versus placebo in 302 subjects with MASH, is considered appropriate to evaluate different doses in the treatment of MASH. In the phase 2 study, MASH was diagnosed appropriately as based on central pathologist evaluation of a recent liver biopsy including NAFLD activity score (NAS) &gt; 4 and fibrosis staging F1-3, resulting in inclusion of patients with a mean age of 55, cardiometabolic indicators (BMI mean 36 kg/m 2 , T2DM 62%) and fibrosis indicators (NAS &gt;4, F1-F3 28% to 49% across categories).

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

According to the hierarchical testing in the dose response study 4296, a statistical significant effect was only found for the 0.4 mg OD dosing for the primary endpoint of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of fibrosis (59% vs 17%, ratio 6.87 [2.60;17,63], p&lt;0.001), while no statistical significant was found for the confirmatory secondary endpoint of improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis (43% vs 33%; ratio 1.42 [0.62;3.28], p=0.2407). Only numerical improvements were observed for the other doses, for the respective endpoints. A post hoc exposureresponse analysis suggests an exposure-related effect on the primary endpoint, with a less clear relation for the confirmatory secondary endpoint. A limitation is that the primary endpoint only aligns with one of the primary endpoints of the phase 3 study, while the secondary endpoint meeting one of the primary endpoints of the pivotal could not demonstrate significance.

A dose-dependent effect for some of the supportive liver-related histological parameters and cardiometabolic markers was observed

It is mentioned that GI events level of at a dose of 0.1-0.2 mg. This would conclude that the highest 0.4 mg OD dose would be the most appropriate dose, and a dose of 2.4 mg once weekly would closest meet the 0.4 mg OD dose.

Based on these considerations, it is considered reasonable to select the 2.4 mg once daily dosing as a maintenance dose with dose escalation to maintenance dose when starting therapy, as the selected dose strategy for the confirmatory pivotal study, although the primary endpoint for the phase 3 deviates from the dose finding study.

## Design and conduct of the clinical studies

In support of the current application, an on-going pivotal phase 3 study provided histological efficacy evidence during the 72 weeks interim period. in 800 subjects with NASH and F2 or F3 (recruitment cap of approximately 20% for subjects with F2).

The general study design of a randomised, placebo-controlled, blinded study was considered appropriate to address the main estimand of the study, to demonstrate that treatment with semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg improves liver histology compared to placebo in subjects with MASH and fibrosis stage 2 or 3. The co-primary endpoints are Resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis , and Improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis , which complied with those defined in the EMA Reflection Paper on MASH ( EMA reflection paper of on regulatory requirements for the development of medicinal products for non-alcoholic steatohepatitis (MASH) (EMA/CHMP/111529/2024)) and the EMA scientific advice. The objective of Part 2 to demonstrate that treatment with semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg lowers the risk of liver-related clinical events compared to placebo in subjects with MASH and fibrosis stage 2 or 3 is considered important to confirm the potential benefits of the currently presented Part 1 interim. However, the large timeframe between Part 1 data and the second part of the study may pose a risk for study integrity.

For the (alpha controlled) key secondary objectives some issues were identified. Resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis as a secondary estimand is likely to highly overlap with one component of the co-primary endpoint/estimand, and in that sense may be of limited value. Further, lowering of body weight is a known effect of semaglutide while there are also other cardiometabolic markers of interest. However, comparing the treatment effects on cardio-metabolic risk factors in subjects with MASH and fibrosis stages 2 or 3 might not support the primary objective evaluation, since it can only show an indirect benefit. A demonstration that treatment with semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg improves patient-reported outcomes could be of direct interest to the patient. However, the general nature of the instrument of Change in SF-36 Bodily Pain does not entirely discriminate whether the changes in score from baseline to 72 weeks may be due to an effect on MASH or due to other related factors, such as reduction in BMI.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Strategies are the same for primary and secondary estimands, except for the continuous outcomes of body weight and SF-36. Here, the intercurrent events of MELD score ≥15, hepatic decompensation events, unplanned biopsy showing progression to cirrhosis, liver transplantation and death were assigned a treatment policy strategy. Although a composite strategy would be better aligned with the primary endpoint, implementation of a composite strategy in continuous endpoints is not straightforward. Considering the relatively low amount of liver-related intercurrent events, the difference between the strategies is likely small and the choice was accepted. It also allows comparison with the endpoints in the weight reduction program.

The intermediate stage of part 1 was set to be based on a fixed number of participants, the first 800 randomised participants. Trial integrity was ensured by using a statistical service provider that was independent of trial conduct and external to the trial sponsor and MAH.

Primary endpoints were analysed with a CMH test, stratifying for the stratification factors. Data handling for the statistical analysis is line with estimand strategies defined above. Missing data was handled by reference-based imputation, which is deemed as conservative for a superiority hypothesis.

Missing data handling was tested using a tipping point analysis, which did not raise any concern about the primary analysis. Nor did a sensitivity analysis using non-response imputation in case of missing data, although this analysis is considered less suitable as it is not conservative when missing data is more prevalent in the comparator arm.

Secondary endpoints measures on a continuous scale were analysed using an ANCOVA, adjusting for the stratification factors.

In the sample size calculation sections, assumptions for treatment difference are specified for the primary and the most important secondary endpoints (so-called confirmatory secondary).

The results of the statistical analyses for the secondary endpoints are agreed.

Strict control of type I error was achieved for all part 1 estimands and the procedure is well described.

Blinding and randomisation were standard and meet general requirements. To meet current general blinding and study conduct criteria, a data monitoring committee independently adjudicate events in a blinded manner following the charter for interim evaluation. According to the DMC charter, the DMC was instructed to recommend unblinding the Novo Nordisk interim team (SIT) to support global regulatory filing when superiority of either one or both primary endpoints was confirmed. The DMC was provided efficacy outputs by an external statistical vendor after the clinical data cut-off. Inclusion of an external event adjudication committee is considered appropriate for a proper evaluation of safety issues. Histological evaluation including central evaluation by a team of two expert histologists and a third when consensus was not reached, is considered rigorous and acceptable.

Inclusion criteria are considered appropriate for selection of the appropriate patient population of informed consented adult patients with stage F2 or F3 MASH. As patients had to have biopsy within 180 days with confirmed stage F2 or F3, and a NAS ≥ 4 with a score of 1 or more in steatosis, lobular inflammation and hepatocyte ballooning, as based on a central pathologist evaluation.

Exclusion criteria are generally considered appropriate. Especially, exclusion of patients with excessive alcohol consumption, meeting any of the defined clinical endpoints, with other possible causes of liver disease, highly elevated liver enzyme, and liver infected diseases, is acceptable. Further, exclusion criteria that could importantly affect study outcome, such as concomitant therapy (GLP-1, vitamin E, pioglitazone), or unstable treatment of associated medication (LLT, glucose lowering medication), signs of uncontrolled diabetes (according to several criteria), and interventions associated with significant obesity change, have been defined. Further, generally known exclusion criteria that potentially could jeopardise study success have appropriately been defined.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Both diabetic and non-diabetic patients were included in the study. During the screening period (V1V2), only HbA1c was measured. From the point of randomisation (V3) onward, HbA1c, fasting plasma glucose (FPG), insulin, glucagon, and HOMA-IR were assessed. The applicant has clarified that the above parameters (HbA1c, FPG, insulin, glucagon, and HOMA-IR) were measured systematically in all participants, irrespective of whether a diagnosis of T2D had been established at screening or diagnosed during trial conduct.

Different injectors have been used in the study, including a single dose and multiple dose injector. These injectors are the same as used for the other indications and bioequivalence between both has been demonstrated. It has been accepted through scientific advice that no additional human factor validation studies were needed for current target population as the target population was considered equally suitable as the T2D and obesity populations.

## Efficacy data and additional analyses

Important protocol deviations were observed, although these were overall comparable between both arms. It was considered that this did not substantially impact study outcome.

A high number of patients (69.5%) were screening failures and 14.7% already withdrew before treatment. Screening failures typically included those not meeting the fibrosis criteria, and uncontrolled diabetes (HbA1c too high). Further, withdrawals consisted of consent by subject, recruitment cap of stage 2 fibrosis, and some others. Of those patients randomised, only a small proportion of patients discontinued, and this was larger in the placebo arm (6.7% vs 18.5%). Semaglutide appears to be well tolerated with only 2.9% vs 3.8% discontinuing due to adverse events, although 12.4% vs 19.5% were not on treatment at the interim Week 72.

Of the 501 (93.8%) semaglutide and 245 (92.1%) placebo patients, only 472 (88.4%) and 225 (84.6%) of the overall population had a biopsy. The applicant has provided details on those with missing biopsies at 72 weeks, which included valid reasons with missing with protocol deviations as most mentioned reason. Among these, subject refusal, and different types of safety concerns, and physician decision of non-improvement were mentioned as examples. Since these were counted as non-responders in the sensitivity analyses, this is considered conservative. Sensitivity analyses and tipping point analyses did not provide different conclusions as to the main findings.

With fairly comparable percentages across important baseline characteristics, randomisation has been successful. A population with certain cardiometabolic disease characteristics has been included in the study with a mean BMI of 35 kg/m 2  and 56% of type 2 diabetes. Weight related disease comorbidities with a large proportion of patients with dysglycemia, hypertension and/or dyslipidemia were noticed. These parameters were reasonably well balanced across the randomised groups. All patients were categorised with Fibrosis stage 2 (21%) or stage 3 (79%) in accordance with baseline inclusion requirements. Moderate enzyme elevation was seen for AST and ALT for about 49% and 68%, respectively, but not for AP (3%). There is sufficient representation of an EU population with 25% of the overall population included. Only 6.3% had a BMI &lt; 25 kg/m 2  and 20.9% with a BMI of 25 to 30 kg/m 2 . The applicant provided baseline characteristics for the subgroup of patients with BMI &lt; 25 kg/m 2 , BMI &lt; 27 kg/m 2  and BMI 25-30 kg/m 2 . For those patients with a BMI &lt; 25 kg/m 2 , these patients were older, more women and more Asian vs White, and less from Europe. This also applies to the BMI 25-30 kg/m 2 , while other baseline characteristics were more or less comparable for these subgroups compared to the entire study population.

Despite the fact that inclusion criteria for the current pivotal study are primarily based on MASH associated criteria and not those as used for approved indications of semaglutide e.g. diabetes and obesity criteria, evidence of efficacy and safety for the population not covered by current approved

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

indications could further support a separate indication of MASH for semaglutide. For the patients with a BMI &lt; 27 kg/m 2 , post-hoc analyses show that weight reduction is also achieved in this subpopulation, as well as for other secondary liver related effects as evaluated in this trial. Any further evidence showing that other factors than weight loss contributed to the treatment effect have not been demonstrated. Nevertheless, a study in China and Taiwan (STEP12) shows in a limited number of 80 patients with a BMI of 24-30 (mean 28 kg/m 2 ) that the greatest reduction was achieved on fat mass instead of lean body mass. These data could also be of support for the EU population with absence of influence on exposure for race and region as derived from phase 3 studies as previously evaluated.

The use of concomitant medication was fairly similar between treatment groups. For some medicinal products this was slightly increased for the placebo-arm, however, not believed to favourably impact the semaglutide arm. 6.8% of the placebo arm patients were treated with semaglutide during the study. All these patients were discontinued study treatment according to protocol but remained in the study for ITT analyses. Reasons for starting this treated were based on prescribed by a physician or suspicion of placebo or lack of effect.

Semaglutide was superior to placebo on both the EMA guideline required intermediate histological endpoints at the pre-planned Week 72 interim of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis (62.9% vs 34.4%; 28.65 %-points [21.09; 36.21]95% CI; p-value &lt;0.0001), and improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis (36.8% vs 22.4%; 14.39 %-points [7.51; 21.27]95% CI; p-value &lt;0.0001). Missing data due to study discontinuation occurred more often in the placebo arm but the number of patients was low. Other reasons for missing data were balanced between study arms. Missing data was handled by reference-based imputation, this will likely have led to a more conservative treatment estimate and therefore does not raise a concern. Sensitivity and supplementary analyses, and consistency across important subgroups of both endpoints, confirmed the robustness of these findings. Especially, consistent findings were observed for the F2 and F3 subgroups, and consistent smaller subgroups of BMI &lt;25 kg/m 2  and 25-30 kg/m 2 , likely not covering populations that fall under the currently already approved indications, in comparison to higher BMIs. Efficacy according to subgroups of &lt; 70 years of age did not reveal important differences with regard to PK, efficacy and safety, while any further subgroup according to age categories of 75-85 and &gt;85 years of age appears not useful due to the low number of patients). Furthermore, as MASH is a slow progressing disease, the relevance of treating patients at older age may be questioned, which has sufficiently addressed in the SmPC.

Hierarchical testing demonstrated statistical significant effect of change in body weight (-10.51 kg vs 2.04 kg; -8.46 %-points [ -9.55; -7.38]95%CI; p-value &lt; 0.0001), resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis (32.7% vs 16.1%; 16.54 [ 10.24; 22.83]95%CI; p-value &lt;0.0001), however not for SF-36 Bodily pain (0.86 vs -0.47; 1.34 [ 0.01; 2.67]95% CI; p-value =0.0488). However, these secondary endpoints may have limitations in support for the primary evaluation as previously discussed.

Of importance for the future assessment of part 2 results, the hypothesis test for SF-36 Bodily plain was not rejected thus no statistical significance can be carried over from part 1 to part 2 of the study.

Nevertheless, also some further support for efficacy based on numerical statistical improvement could be derived from other (exploratory) secondary endpoints of MASH/liver related endpoints including steatohepatitis with at least a 2-point reduction in NAS and no worsening of fibrosis, histologyassessed liver collagen proportionate area, worsening in steatohepatitis, improvement in histologyassessed ballooning, improvement in histology-assessed inflammation, improvement in histologyassessed steatosis, MASH resolution (ballooning of 0, inflammation of 01) and ≥2 -point NAS reduction with no worsening of fibrosis, progression of liver fibrosis in patients with F2, and progression of liver fibrosis. Further, imaging-based endpoints also provided some suggestion for efficacy based on

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

numerical statistical improvements in liver stiffness assessed by FibroScan, CAP values assessed by transient elastography (FibroScan), and FibroScan-AST score. Also, efficacy based on numerical statistical improvements was observed for liver enzymes including ALT and AST, although these were only moderately elevated for about half of the patients. Other blood biomarkers of type-iii collagen through Pro-C3 score and Enhanced Liver Fibrosis score also showed numerical improvements.

Several other cardiometabolic makers other than body weight reduction and known to be associated with semaglutide treatment have been evaluated including diabetes markers, lipid markers, and inflammation markers. In line with known mechanisms of semaglutide, numerical improvements were observed for HbA1c and on the exploratory marker of insulin sensitivity (through HOMA-IR), in diabetic patients but also the non-diabetic patients. While the lipid profile was close to the normal range, slight numerical improvements could be seen for semaglutide vs placebo for changes in triglycerides, free fatty acids, LDL-C, and HDL-C. Suggestion for inflammation reduction could be observed for hsCRP, and on exploratory markers including TNF-alpha and IL-1R antagonist. Still, the clinical meaning of these observations is considered not entirely clear. Discontinuation based solely on weight reduction is likely not appropriate considering that other factors also contribute to the overall treatment effect.

The impact on patient reported outcome is somewhat unclear. While patient reported outcome of the hierarchical tested secondary endpoint of SF-36 Bodily pain could not demonstrate significance, and NASH-CHECK abdominal pain was not numerically improved, some suggestion for efficacy based on numerical improvement could be observed for the SF-36 Physical Component, SF-36 Mental Component.

With regard to immunogenicity findings, three patients developed detectable ADA responses, with antibody titres ranging from 15 to 120 and a median titre of 30.

The subjects did not exhibit extreme obesity or atypical metabolic characteristics, and their baseline profiles were comparable to the general study population, excluding any identifiable metabolic or phenotypic factors contributing to altered immunogenicity. The description that no clinical, pharmacokinetic, or pharmacodynamic impact was observed further supports the lack of clinical relevance of these antibody findings.

Overall, the available evidence would support a conditional marketing authorisation in accordance with the EMA reflection paper of on regulatory requirements for the development of medicinal products for MASH (EMA/CHMP/111529/2024). Interim findings on intermediate histological endpoints and some other markers possible associated with liver disease should ultimately show to translate into clinical improvement. Therefore, evidence on clinical endpoints should be delivered as a specific obligation, as currently planned with the conduct of the second part of the on-going pivotal study. Clinical evidence is currently defined based on a combined endpoint of histological progression to cirrhosis, all cause death, liver induced MELD score ≥ 15, liver transplantation, or hepatic decompensation events.

## 5.3.10.2. Conclusions on the clinical efficacy

In the pivotal study including patients with biopsy confirmed MASH and fibrosis stage 2 and 3, semaglutide demonstrated a significant beneficial effect at 72 weeks on the interim co-primary endpoints of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis (62.9% vs 34.4%; 28.65 %-points [21.09; 36.21]95% CI; p-value &lt;0.0001), and improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis (36.8% vs 22.4%; 14.39 %-points [7.51; 21.27]95% CI; p-value &lt;0.0001) compared to placebo. Hierarchical tested secondary endpoints of change in body weight, resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis showed beneficial effects, however, this was not the case for the patient reported SF-36 Bodily pain endpoint. Further, support of these endpoints for the primary endpoint may be limited. Nevertheless, other histological, imaging, plasma

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

derived liver markers, cardiometabolic markers, and inflammation markers generally support the beneficial effect of semaglutide.

However, clinical endpoint evaluation is still needed to confirm the interim histological benefits, which are intended to be gathered with the on-going study to obtain full approval.

## 5.4. Clinical safety

Please refer to the table of studies in section 5.3.2.

For the purpose of this document, the following definitions apply:

'Adverse event - AE' means any untoward medical occurrence in a subject to whom a medicinal product is administered, and which does not necessarily have a causal relationship with this treatment.

'Serious adverse event - SAE' means any untoward medical occurrence that at any dose requires inpatient hospitalisation or prolongation of existing hospitalisation, results in persistent or significant disability or incapacity, results in a congenital anomaly or birth defect, is life-threatening, or results in death. The definition (in line with ICH E2A) includes important medical events that may not be immediately life-threatening or result in death or hospitalisation but may jeopardise the patient or may require intervention to prevent one of the other outcomes listed in the definition above.

'Adverse drug reaction - ADR' means any untoward and unintended response to a medicinal product related to any dose administered, for which, after a thorough assessment, a causal relationship between the medicinal product and the adverse event is at least a reasonable possibility, based for example, on their comparative incidence in clinical trials, or findings from epidemiological studies and/or on an evaluation of causality from individual case reports.

## 5.4.1. Safety data collection

The clinical development programme for semaglutide 2.4 mg for MASH includes 4 trials, pivotal phase 3a trial 4553 (ESSENCE) in a population with biopsy-confirmed MASH F2-F3, and 3 supportive studies, phase 2 dose finding trial 4296 in a population with MASH F1-F3, phase 2 trial 4492 in a population of subjects with biopsy-defined MASH and compensated cirrhosis (F4c) and one clinical pharmacology trial 4381 in a population of subjects with NAFLD and increased liver stiffness (Table 29).

The safety data from on-going study 4553 are based on a predefined interim analysis set on subject #800 reaching the week-72 visit window, as per the data cut-off date of 05 September 2024. Because the trials are heterogeneous with respect to treatment regimen (dose levels and dosing frequency), trial populations, and duration of exposure for subjects contributing to the safety-related evaluations, data from each trial are evaluated and presented separately.

The present application is based on data and results from an interim evaluation of trial 4553 (part 1). The SAS (interim) includes all subjects exposed to a least one dose of trial product up until the interim data cut-off date. |

The safety evaluation of semaglutide 2.4 mg in subjects with MASH presented in this summary builds upon the compiled knowledge of safety with semaglutide from earlier development programmes, as well as post-marketing data. At the time of data-cut off, post marketing data covered approximately 20 million patients treated for the approved indications for Ozempic, Rybelsus and Wegovy.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Safety data analysis methodology

## Safety analysis dataset

The SAS includes all subjects who have been exposed to at least one dose of trial product.

Observations periods

- The in-trial observation period is defined as the time period where the subject is followed in the trial and ends at the first of the following dates, end-of-trial visit for completed trials; follow-up visit for subjects who have withdrawn, last visit prior to the interim data cut-off date (trial 4553 only), last contact with subject (for subjects lost to follow-up), or death.
- The on-treatment observation period is defined as the time period where the subject is treated with trial product. The on-treatment period begins on the date of first dose of trial product and ends after a follow-up period following the last dose, of 7 weeks for AEs, adjudicated events and hypoglycaemic episodes, and of 1 week (7 days) for laboratory assessments, and physical examination.

The aggregated duration of the in-trial and on-treatment observation periods are given in patient years of observation (PYO) and patient years of exposure (PYE), respectively. Additionally, in trial 4553, the patient years at risk of incident event (PYI) is used for safety evaluations, where time at risk is defined as the duration from randomisation until the first event or the end of the observation period, whichever comes first.

In general, safety evaluations will be based SAS (interim) or SAS and the on-treatment period as the primary safety data cut. The in-trial observation period is used for safety areas concerning 'use in pregnancy and during lactation' (pre-defined MedDRA searches on neonatal exposures via breast milk, and fertility disorders with potential long latency between onset and diagnosis). Safety focus areas will be summarised for both the in-trial and on-treatment observation periods.

## Safety assessments and data collection

For trial 4553, the schedule of safety (AE) visits was every 2 weeks the first four weeks, thereafter every fourth week up to week 16 and increasingly longer visit windows from week 16. For trials 4296, 4492 and 4381, the schedule of safety (AE) visits were every 2 weeks for at least 12 weeks and thereafter every 4-12 weeks until end-of trial.

AEs were collected via investigator reporting. Adverse events (AEs) will be summarised by the number of subjects with at least one event, proportion of subjects with at least one event, number of events, event rate based on exposure or observation time (number of events per 100 person-years of exposure or observation (PYE/PYO)), and incidence based on time at risk (number of events per 100 person-years at risk (PYI)).

In trials 4553 and 4296, blinded adjudication of selected event types was performed on an ongoing basis by an independent, external event adjudication committee (EAC). In both trials, types of AEs to be sent for adjudication were pre-specified, as presented in Table 29.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Safety focus areas

Based on the therapeutic experience with GLP-1 RAs and regulatory feedback and requirements, safety focus areas were pre-defined as being of special interest in the evaluation of the safety of semaglutide 2.4 mg for MASH: Gastrointestinal disorders, Hepatic disorders, Gallbladder-related disorders, Acute pancreatitis, Cardiovascular disorders, Neoplasms, Acute renal failure, Hypoglycaemia, Retinal disorders, Immunogenicity, Psychiatric disorders, Rare events, Medication errors, drug abuse or misuse, and overdose, Suspected transmission of an infectious agent via trial product, COVID-19.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Study 4553

A total of 1195 subjects were randomised to receive semaglutide 2.4 mg once weekly (n=800) or placebo (n=395). At the time of the interim evaluation, 800 subjects were treated with semaglutide, with 643 subjects treated for at least 6 months, and a total of 542 subjects treated for at least 12 months. At time of the interim evaluation, the mean (SD) exposure time for subjects in SAS (interim) was 85.7 (50.4) weeks for the on-treatment observation period, 87.1 (50.7) weeks on semaglutide, and 82.8 (49.9) weeks on placebo.

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 A total of 320 subjects were randomised to receive semaglutide 0.1 mg (80 subjects), semaglutide 0.2 mg (78 subjects), semaglutide 0.4 mg (82 subjects), or placebo (80 subjects). All randomised subjects except one (in the semaglutide 0.4 mg group) were exposed to trial product. The total exposure time in the treatment groups ranged from 105.8 years to 115.4 years (on-treatment period) and the total observation time ranged from 112.2 years to 119.6 years (in-trial period), with the lowest values in the semaglutide 0.2 mg group (both periods).

Study 4492 A total of 71 subjects were randomised to receive semaglutide 2.4 mg (47 subjects) or placebo (24 subjects). The total on-treatment patient years of exposure (PYE) in the semaglutide group (46.0 years) and the placebo group (24.6 years) reflected the 2:1 randomisation ratio.

Study 4381 A total of 66 subjects were exposed to trial product, of these 33 subjects were exposed to semaglutide 0.4 mg once daily, following dose escalation from 0.05 mg/day up to 0.4 mg mg/day. The total mean (SD) on-treatment observation period was 73.0 (16.8) weeks. The mean (SD) number of treatment weeks per subject in the semaglutide arm was 71.9 (17.6) and 74.0 (16.1) in the placebo arm.

## 5.4.3. Adverse events

## Overall incidence of Adverse Events

## Study 4553

Overall, the proportions of subjects who experienced AEs, as well as the event rates, were higher with semaglutide 2.4 mg (86.3%, 407.1 events per 100 PYE) than with placebo (78.7%; 303.0 events per 100 PYE). This treatment difference was largely driven by the higher proportions of subjects with gastrointestinal AEs (mainly nausea, diarrhoea, constipation and vomiting) in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group (Table 33).

The majority of AEs were non-serious, and mild or moderate in severity across both treatment groups. The subjects reporting events were primarily reported as recovered or not recovered at the time of the interim evaluation. AEs leading to premature discontinuation of trial product were reported by a low proportion of subjects, with comparable proportion of subjects between semaglutide 2.4 mg and placebo.

The majority of events were assessed as unlikely related to trial product in both treatment groups. A higher proportion of subjects reported events assessed as probably or possibly related to trial product with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo, this was driven by gastrointestinal AEs.

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 The proportions of subjects who experienced AEs, as well as the event rates, were higher in each of the semaglutide groups (90.0%-97.4%; 447.6-545.4 events per 100 PYE) than in the placebo group (83.8%; 391.4 events per 100 PYE). The highest proportion of subjects who experienced AEs, as well as the event rates, were seen in the semaglutide 0.2 mg group. The difference in the proportions of subjects with AEs between the semaglutide groups and the placebo group appeared to be largely driven by the higher proportions of subjects with gastrointestinal AEs (mainly nausea, constipation, diarrhoea, vomiting, and abdominal pain) in the semaglutide groups. Across treatment groups, the majority of AEs were non-serious, mild in severity and with the outcome resolved.

The proportion of subjects with AEs leading to premature treatment discontinuation was higher in the semaglutide 0.2 mg group (12.8%) than in the other treatment groups including placebo (ranging between 3.8% and 5.0%). Gastrointestinal disorders were the most common reason for discontinuation among subjects who received semaglutide (1.3%-7.7% of the subjects); no subjects in the placebo group discontinued because of gastrointestinal disorders.

A larger percentage of AEs in the semaglutide groups (approximately 31% to 46% of all AEs) than in the placebo group (20% of all AEs) were judged by the investigator as possibly or probably related to trial product, driven by gastrointestinal AEs.

AEs were reported throughout the trial in all treatment groups, however, in the semaglutide groups, 80% or more of the subjects had their first event within the first 24 weeks of treatment.

Time to onset of first event

Time to onset of any event

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Study 4492 AEs were reported by 89.4% of subjects in the semaglutide group treated with 2.4 mg once weekly (630.5 events per 100 PYE) compared to 79.2% of the subjects in the placebo group (345.1 events per 100 PYE). Event rates in the semaglutide group were primarily driven by gastrointestinal AEs. The majority of the AEs in the two treatment groups were of mild or moderate severity. Slightly more severe AEs were seen in the semaglutide group compared to placebo, though based on low numbers, in 17% versus 4.2 % of subjects. SAEs were reported by 12.8% (corresponding to 6 subjects) in the semaglutide group and 8.3% (corresponding to 2 subjects) in the placebo group.

Study 4381 AEs were reported by 93.9% of subjects in the semaglutide group (464.0 events per 100 PYE) compared to 87.9% of the subjects in the placebo group (303.3 events per 100 PYE). Proportions and event rates in the semaglutide group appeared to be largely driven by gastrointestinal AEs. The majority of the AEs in the two treatment groups were of mild or moderate severity, and severe AEs were reported in 12.1% versus 9.1%. Study drug was withdrawn in 1(3.0%) subject on semaglutide, and dose was reduced in 2 (6.1%), and outcome was reported as recovered in 93.9% of subjects. More SAEs were reported in the semaglutide s.c. 0.4 mg arm (12.1%, 6 events in 4 subjects) than in the placebo arm (9.1%, 3 events in 3 subjects).

## Semaglutide 2.4 mg for weight management

Overall, the AE reporting was similar between trial 4553 (interim evaluation) and the clinical development programme for Wegovy (see SmPC).

## Common adverse events Study 4553

The most frequently reported AEs belonged to the SOC Gastrointestinal disorders with a higher proportion of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg reporting gastrointestinal AEs compared to placebo (69.5% versus 46.8%). AEs within the SOCs Infections and infestations, Musculoskeletal and connective tissue disorders, General disorders and administration site conditions, Metabolism and nutrition disorders and Nervous system disorders were also frequently reported (by at least 20% of the subjects in any treatment group).

With the exception of Gastrointestinal disorders, the proportion of subjects reporting AEs within the different SOCs were generally comparable across treatment groups (Figure 15).

Figure 16: AEs by PT -most frequent ( ≥ 10%) -on treatment -SAS (interim) -trial 4553

<!-- image -->

·

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Among the most frequently reported AEs, nausea, diarrhoea, constipation and vomiting belonging to the SOC Gastrointestinal disorders were all more frequently reported in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group compared to the placebo group (18.5%-36.1% versus 5.6%-12.4%). These types of events are well known for semaglutide and for the GLP-1 RA class in general. The PT decreased appetite belonging to the SOC Metabolism and nutrition disorders was reported more often with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo (14.0% versus 2.5%).

AEs reported by ≥ 5% and by a higher proportion of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo are: Dyspepsia: 7.6 % versus 2.8%; Abdominal distension: 7.5% versus 3.5%; Gastrooesophageal reflux disease: 7.4% versus 1.5%; Eructation: 5.3% versus 0.8%; Back pain: 6.1% versus 4.1%; Headache: 8.0% versus 6.3%; and Fatigue: 8.9% versus 5.3%. The majority of events were non-serious and all mild or moderate in severity. Most events were unlikely related to trial product, did not lead to premature trial product discontinuation and approximately half resolved. There was 1 SAE of back pain (worsening). The event did not lead to any changes in dose, resolved and was assessed as unlikely related to trial product.

AEs reported by ≥ 2% and by a higher proportion of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo are: Flatulence: 3.6% versus 2.5%; Alopecia: 3.0% versus 0.5%; Lipase increased: 2.5% versus 1.0%; Weight decreased: 4.4% versus 0.8%; Gastroenteritis: 4.0% versus 1.8%; Muscle spasms: 2.5% versus 1.0%; Insomnia: 4.1% versus 1.8%; Fall: 2.1% versus 0.8%. All events were non-serious, and mild or moderate in severity except one SAE of PT fall that led to treatment discontinuation and none led to treatment discontinuation. Most of the events were resolved at time of the interim evaluation of trial 4553 and assessed as unlikely related to trial product.

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 The most frequently reported AEs in all treatment groups belonged to the SOC Gastrointestinal disorders with the highest proportions of subjects reporting gastrointestinal AEs in the semaglutide groups (63.8%-76.9% versus 45.0% in the placebo group). AEs within the SOCs Infections and infestations, Nervous system disorders, Metabolism and nutrition disorders, Musculoskeletal and connective tissue disorders, General disorders and administration site conditions, Injury, poisoning and procedural complications, and Investigations were also frequently reported in all treatment groups (by at least 20% of the subjects in any treatment group), and by overall similar proportions of subjects across treatment groups.

A higher proportion of subjects in the semaglutide groups than in the placebo group reported AEs within the SOC Skin and subcutaneous tissue disorders (12.3%-21.8% versus 7.5%) and the SOC Neoplasms, benign, malignant and unspecified (6.3%-7.4% versus 2.5%). AEs related to neoplasms were mostly benign, non-serious and mild in severity. A total of 3 malignant neoplasms in the semaglutide 0.1 mg and 0.2 mg groups were reported. These affected different organs and were all assessed by the investigator as unlikely related to trial product. A lower proportion of subjects in the semaglutide groups than in the placebo group reported AEs within the SOC Renal and urinary disorders (7.4%-8.8% versus 15.0%).

An overview of the most frequently reported AEs by PT reported by ≥10% of the subjects in any treatment group is provided in Figure 17. Among the most frequently reported AEs, nausea, constipation, decreased appetite, diarrhoea, vomiting and abdominal pain (SOCs Gastrointestinal disorders and Metabolism and nutrition disorders) were all more frequently reported in the semaglutide groups than in the placebo group. Other frequently reported AEs, back pain, nasopharyngitis, arthralgia, and fatigue - were reported by comparable proportions of subjects across treatment groups, without noteworthy differences between the treatment groups.

In the supportive trials 4492 and 4381 , including subjects with MASH F4c and subjects with NAFLD and increased liver stiffness, AEs reported by ≥10% of the subjects in any treatment group were all non-serious events, and the majority of events were mild to moderate in severity. The most frequent PTs were nausea, diarrhoea, vomiting and decreased appetite.

## Semaglutide 2.4 mg for weight-management

The most frequently reported adverse reactions were gastrointestinal disorders including nausea, diarrhoea, constipation and vomiting. AEs and observed treatment differences between semaglutide 2.4 mg and placebo were similar to results in study 4553. In the semaglutide 2.4 mg group the PTs headache, dysgeusia and diabetic retinopathy were reported by a lower proportion of subjects with MASH compared to subjects with overweight or obesity (Wegovy), and the PTs increased lipase and delayed gastric emptying were reported by a higher proportion of subjects with MASH compared to subjects with overweight or obesity (Wegovy).

## Adverse Events by severity

## Study 4553

The majority of AEs were non-serious, in 85.5% of subjects on semaglutide vs 77.0 % of subjects on placebo. Most AEs were graded as mild or moderate (in 80.3% vs 72.7%, and 47.8% vs 42.8% of subjects on semaglutide vs placebo, respectively), and only a limited proportion of AEs was graded severe, with no imbalance for semaglutide vs placebo, 8.9% vs 8.4%.

## Supportive studies

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Study 4296 Across treatment groups, the majority of AEs were non-serious, mild in severity and with the outcome resolved. There were more SAEs in the semaglutide groups compared to placebo (ranging from 14.8% to 19.2% vs 10.0%). There was no apparent dose-relationship among the semaglutide groups with regards to the proportion of subjects with serious or severe AEs, or with AEs with outcome not resolved.

Study 4492 The majority of the AEs in the two treatment groups were of mild or moderate severity. Slightly more severe AEs were seen in the semaglutide group compared to placebo, though based on low numbers.

Study 4381 The majority of AEs, in both treatment groups, occurred primarily in the first 24 weeks of the trial, were non-serious, mild or moderate in severity, with outcomes of recovered or recovering.

## Adverse events by relationship to study medication

## Study 4553

Probably or possibly related treatment-emergent adverse events were reported with higher frequency on semaglutide, in 549 (68.6%) vs 161 (40.8%) subjects.

Most probably or possibly treatment-related adverse events reported more frequently on semaglutide 2.4 mg belonged to the SOC Gastrointestinal disorders, in 482 (60.3%) vs 122 (30.9) subjects, including nausea (34.1% vs 10.9%), diarrhoea (20.3% vs 10.4%), constipation (17.3% vs 5.3%), vomiting (15.9% vs 3.3%), dyspepsia (6.9% vs 2.3%), abdominal distention (6.5% vs 2.5%), and gastrooesophageal reflux disease (5.9% vs 0.5%). Also, decreased appetite (13.6% vs 2.3%), fatigue (6.4% vs 2.8%), headache (4.9% vs 3.0 %), and weight decreased (4.1% vs 0.5%) were reported ( CSR study 4553 ).

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 The proportion of subjects with AEs judged by the investigator as possibly or probably related to trial product was higher in the semaglutide groups (in 60.0%, 73.1% and 71.6% of the subjects in the semaglutide 0.1 mg, 0.2 mg and 0.4 mg groups, respectively) than in the placebo group (48.8%), mainly belonged to the SOC Gastrointestinal disorders (45.0%, 61.5%, and 54.3%, versus 28.8% in the placebo group). AEs assessed as being related to treatment were graded serious in 2.5%, 3.8% and 2.5% on semaglutide 0.1 mg, 0.2 mg and 0.4 mg, versus 1.3% on placebo. Severe treatment related AEs were reported in 6.3%, 5.1%, and 4.9% versus 1.3% of subjects. The semaglutide dose was reduced in 0, 1.3% and 3.7% of subjects on semaglutide versus 0 on placebo, and study drug was withdrawn in 2.5%, 10.3%, and 3.7% of subjects on semaglutide versus 5.0 of subjects on placebo.

Study 4492 The proportion of subjects with AEs judged by the investigator as possibly or probably related to trial product was higher in the semaglutide group (78.7%) than in the placebo group (45.8%), mainly due to events in the SOC Gastrointestinal disorders (70.2% in the semaglutide group versus 25.0% in the placebo group). All AEs assessed as being related to treatment were non-serious and none were severe, with outcomes of recovered/recovering in most events.

Study 4381 The proportion of subjects with AEs judged by the investigator as possibly or probably related to trial product was higher in the semaglutide s.c. 0.4 mg arm (84.8%) than in the placebo arm (54.5%). This was mainly due to the greater number of GI related AEs assessed as being related to trial product in the semaglutide arm (60.6%) than the placebo arm (30.3%). All AEs assessed as being related to treatment were non-serious, and most were mild (78.8% on semaglutide vs 51.5% on

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

placebo). The semaglutide dose was reduced in 2 cases. None of the AEs assessed as possibly/probably related to treatment resulted in withdrawals from the trial.

During trial conduct, AEs were collected via investigator reporting and the investigator was to assess the AE with regards to relationship to trial product (probable, possible or unlikely). AEs for which a causal relation with semaglutide was judged by the investigator as at least a reasonable possibility, were proposed to be included in section 4.8 of the SmPC as Adverse Drug Reactions. In addition to AEs reported in pivotal study 4553 (ESSENCE) in the target population at the target dose of 2.4 mg once weekly that are judged as possibly or probably related to semaglutide, also ADRs reported in studies on Wegovy 2.4 mg once weekly in weight management are included in the listing of adverse events.

## 5.4.4.1. Gastro-intestinal disorders

Gastrointestinal AEs are the most common adverse reactions reported with GLP-1 RAs, hence considered a class effect for all GLP-1 RAs. The precise mechanism remains unclear, but it involves an activation of the GLP-1 receptor. The frequency of gastrointestinal AEs is known to be dependent on the GLP-1 RA dose level, which may be mitigated by following the intended dose escalation scheme. MASH is closely associated with metabolic abnormalities, such as obesity, which appears to be associated with a higher frequency of certain gastrointestinal disorders e.g., upper abdominal pain, gastroesophageal reflux disease, diarrhoea, vomiting and haemorrhoids.

Gastrointestinal AEs are evaluated based on a pre-defined MedDRA search using the on-treatment observation period.

## Study 4553

·

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Gastrointestinal AEs were reported by a higher proportion of subjects and at higher event rates for semaglutide 2.4 mg (69.5%, 185.7 events per 100 PYE) compared to placebo (46.8%, 72.2 events per 100 PYE) (Table 34). The majority of gastrointestinal AEs were non-serious, and mild or moderate in severity. Overall, the majority of events were reported within the dose-escalation period. For events of nausea, most subjects reported their first event during the dose-escalation period; however, events of nausea were reported throughout the trial duration in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group. Nausea increased dose-dependently across the semaglutide groups, whereas no clear dose relationship was observed for diarrhoea, vomiting or constipation. Estimated median durations were comparable between semaglutide 2.4 mg and placebo for nausea, diarrhoea and vomiting, whereas for constipation, the median duration was longer with semaglutide 2.4 mg than with placebo. The majority of the AEs were reported as recovered or resolved and judged by the investigator to be either possibly or probably related to trial product. Gastrointestinal AEs were assessed as possibly or probably related to trial product for a larger proportion of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo (75.3% vs 36.5%).

Most common PTs are defined as reported by ≥10% of subjects in one of the treatment groups. Values for PYI (patient-years at risk of incident event) and I (incidence [number of incident events per 100 PYI]) are available in the TFL.

The most common PTs reported were nausea, diarrhoea, vomiting and constipation. AEs related to gastroparesis (PT: impaired gastric emptying) were reported by 8 subjects (1.0%, 9 events) with semaglutide 2.4 mg and 1 subject (0.3%, 1 event) with placebo. All but one of the events were nonserious, and all events were mild or moderate in severity. The outcomes for these events were reported as not resolved for 6 subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg and for the one event with placebo. For pre-defined grouped PTs for abdominal pain, gastritis, and intestinal obstruction the proportions of subjects reporting events were comparable between semaglutide 2.4 mg and placebo. These grouped

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

PTs have previously been reported by a higher number of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo in the semaglutide 2.4 mg for weight management (Wegovy).

SAEs of gastrointestinal disorders were reported by 2.5% of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg and 1.5% of subjects with placebo, these were spread across multiple PTs.

The majority of AEs were reported during the dose escalation period; however, events of nausea were reported throughout the trial duration in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group.

The number of gastrointestinal AEs leading to premature discontinuation of trial product were low in both treatment groups, reported by 1.6% of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg and 0.5% of subjects with placebo.

## Supportive studies

In study 4296, the proportion of subjects reporting gastrointestinal disorders ranged between 63.8%-76.9% in the semaglutide group versus 45.0% in the placebo group. The majority of gastrointestinal AEs were non-serious, and mild in severity. The most frequent PTs were nausea, diarrhoea, vomiting and constipation; all reported by greater proportions of subjects and at higher rates in the semaglutide groups than in the placebo group. The proportion of subjects who reported nausea increased dose-dependently across the semaglutide groups, whereas no clear dose relationship was observed for diarrhoea, vomiting or constipation.

## 5.4.4.2. Hepatic disorders

Hepatotoxicity and drug-induced liver injury (DILI) are important regulatory focus points for new drugs targeting MASH, hence hepatic disorders are assessed as a safety focus area. Marketed GLP-1 RAs are not known to be hepatotoxic and there have been no indications of treatment-related liver toxicity in the non-clinical toxicology studies with semaglutide. Semaglutide is metabolised by enzymes widely distributed throughout the body, with no single organ seen as responsible for the metabolism. The GLP-1 receptors have not been detected on liver cells.

AE evaluations are based on the in-trial period for trial 4553 and the on-treatment period for the clinical pharmacology and phase 2 trials. Event adjudication of selected AEs, including AEs related to hepatic decompensation, liverinduced MELD score ≥15 and potential DILI events is performed by an independent, blinded external event adjudication committee.

Definition of DILI . In general, liver injury is defined as alanine aminotransferase (ALT) or aspartate aminotransferase (AST) ≥3 x ULN and total bilirubin ≥2 x ULN where no alternative aetiology exists (Hy's law). In the clinical programme, for subjects with elevated AST and ALT levels at baseline potential DILI was defined by per protocol as AST/ALT&gt;=2 or &gt;=300 U/L).

## Study 4553

In trial 4553 (interim evaluation), hepatic events were reported by comparable proportions of subjects and event rates for semaglutide 2.4 mg (5.0%, 4.3 events per 100 PYO) compared to placebo (7.8%, 7.6 events per 100 PYO) (Table 37). The majority of the events were non-serious and mild or moderate in severity. None of the events led to premature treatment discontinuation in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group. The most commonly reported PTs were related to elevated laboratory values, these were reported by a lower proportion of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg than with placebo, for ALT (0.4% and 2.0%, respectively) and AST (0.3% and 1.3%, respectively), and with comparable proportion of subjects across treatment groups for GGT (0.5% and 0.5%, respectively),

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

bilirubin (0.6% and 0.3%, respectively), INR (0.8% and 1.5%, respectively) and MELD score (0.3% and 0.5%,respectively).

Hepatic disorders based on liver-related laboratory parameters . At baseline, a large proportion of subjects had elevated levels of ALT (56% on semaglutide vs 56.4% on placebo) and/or AST (76.5% vs 77%). ALT and AST values decreased from baseline to week 72 in both treatment groups (Table 38). The reductions were greater with semaglutide 2.4 mg than with placebo and occurred within the first 36 weeks. The mean level of ALP decreased from baseline to week 72 in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group, with no change in the placebo group. Mean values of total bilirubin, albumin and INR, and MELD score remained stable over time in both treatment groups.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Drug-Induced-Liver-Injury . Per protocol definition there were no cases of Hy's law. One (1) case of biochemical Hy ' s law (AST ≥ 3 × ULN + TBL ≥ 2 × ULN) was identified based on data from an unscheduled visit. However, this subject had elevated AST and ALT levels at baseline and therefore did not fulfil the per protocol defined cutoff for potential drug-induced liver injury for subjects with elevated levels at baseline (AST/ALT ≥2x baseline level or ≥300 U/L with concurrent total bilirubin ≥2xULN). Throughout the trial normal fluctuations in liver-related values were observed for the subject and values normalised under treatment without any changes to trial product.

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 The proportion of subjects reporting hepatic events ranged between 7.7% and 11.3% in the semaglutide groups versus 13.8% in the placebo group. All reported hepatic events were non serious and mild or moderate in severity. For the majority of events the outcome was reported as resolved. Overall, the events were distributed across multiple PTs (mainly blood bilirubin increased, hepatic enzyme increased, and INR increased) with few events reported for each PT. Only increased blood bilirubin was reported by a slightly higher proportion of subjects in the semaglutide 0.1 mg (3.8%) and 0.4 mg (3.7%) groups (no events in 0.2 mg group) than in the placebo group (1.3%). One (1) subject (in the semaglutide 0.2 mg group) had 1 event of the PT hepatitis acute that led to premature treatment discontinuation. Two events led to treatment discontinuation in the placebo group. The proportions of subjects who had abnormal liver values during the trial were generally lower in the semaglutide groups than in the placebo group, and no cases fulfilling biochemical Hy's Law were identified.

Study 4492 In this study in subjects with biopsy-defined MASH and compensated cirrhosis (F4c), a total of 10 hepatic events in 6 subjects were reported: 9 events in 5 subjects in the semaglutide group (2 cased of ascites, in one case after study treatment discontinuation, and single cases of increased bilirubin, AST, ALT, GGT, MELD score increased to 12, portal hypertensive gastropathy and oesphageal varices) and 1 event in the placebo group (hepatic lesion following liver biopsy). All of the events were non serious, and mild or moderate in severity. None of the events led to premature treatment discontinuation. Mean values for the liver enzymes ALT and AST decreased from baseline to week 48 in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and remained stable in the placebo group. No cases of biochemical Hy's Law were identified.

Study 4381 A total of 7 hepatic events were reported: 2 events in one subject in the semaglutide 0.4 mg group, and 5 events in 4 subjects in the placebo group. All events were non serious and mild in severity, and the outcome was reported as recovered/recovering for all subjects. All reported events were related to elevated liver parameters (ALT, AST or INR). Mean values for the liver parameters AST, ALT and GGT were assessed as efficacy parameters, these all decreased more with semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo.

## 5.4.4.3. Gall-bladder related disorders

Gallbladder-related disorders such as gallstones (cholelithiasis) are associated with metabolic risk factors, including NAFLD, with a bidirectional relationship between the incidence of NAFLD and gallstones. Additional risk factors include obesity (especially central obesity, which is closely related to MASH), female gender, and rapid and large weight loss. Gallstones may lead to complications such as cholecystitis and acute pancreatitis. GLP-1 RA treatment has been associated with increased risks of gallbladder or biliary diseases. The risk was dose dependent and increased with longer duration of GLP1 RA use. Acute gallstone disease (cholelithiasis) is considered a class risk for GLP-1 RA products.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Study 4553

In trial 4553 (interim evaluation), AEs of the known risk, gallbladder-related disorders, were reported by 2.5% of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg (1.9 events per 100 PYE) compared to 1.5% of subjects with placebo (1.1 events per 100 PYE). This was consistent with previous trials with semaglutide 2.4 mg (Wegovy). The majority of events were non-serious, mild in severity and unlikely related to trial product. Approximately 2/3 of the events in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and half of the events in the placebo group were resolved or resolving. None of the events led to premature trial product discontinuation

The most frequently reported PT was cholelithiasis, which was reported by 1.4% of subjects with semaglutide 2.4 mg and 0.8% of subjects with placebo. Five (5) subjects in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 1 subject in the placebo group reported blood bilirubin increased. The remaining events were distributed across multiple PTs with single events reported for each.

Events of symptomatic acute gallbladder disease were reported in 5 subjects with a total of 6 events in the semaglutide 2.4 group and 2 subjects with a total of 3 events in the placebo group. A total of 3 SAEs (PTs cholangitis acute, cholecystitis and cholelithiasis) were reported by 2 subjects, 1 in each treatment group. All 3 events resolved.

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 The proportion of subjects reporting gallbladder-related disorders ranged between 5.1%7.4% in the semaglutide groups versus 2.5% in the placebo group. The majority of the events were non-serious and mild or moderate in severity. Approximately half of the events were judged by the investigator as unlikely related to trial product. The most frequently reported gallbladder-related AE was blood bilirubin increased. In total, 5 SAEs were reported by 3 subjects, all in the semaglutide groups; of these, 1 led to treatment discontinuation, the other 4 led to treatment interruption.

## 5.4.4.4. Acute pancreatitis

Acute pancreatitis is considered a class risk associated with the use of GLP-1 RA, and subjects with a history pancreatitis or with recent acute pancreatitis were excluded from participating in the trials. In addition, trial product was to be discontinued in case of suspicion of acute pancreatitis during trial conduct. Increases in amylase and lipase levels are well known from GLP-1 RAs including semaglutide. The exact mechanism behind this observation is at present unknown but may be attributed to the pharmacological effects of GLP-1 RAs on the pancreatic acini.

## Study 4553

In trial 4553 (interim evaluation), there were few AEs related to acute pancreatitis. AEs of acute pancreatitis were reported by comparable proportions of subjects and event rates with semaglutide 2.4 mg (0.4%, 0.2 events per 100 PYE) compared to placebo (0.5%, 0.3 events per 100 PYE). One event was moderate, the rest were mild in severity. All events resolved. Reported PTs were either pancreatitis acute or pancreatitis.

In total, 3 SAEs (all PT pancreatitis acute) were reported, 2 in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 1 in the placebo group. All 3 events were considered possibly related to trial product and led to either trial product discontinuation or interruption. All 3 events resolved.

Pancreatic enzymes . Amylase and lipase levels increased from baseline to week 72 with semaglutide 2.4 mg. The increase was most pronounced during the first 12 weeks. There was no change from baseline in the placebo group.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

For amylase increased few events were reported and the proportion of subjects reporting events as well as event rates were comparable between semaglutide 2.4 mg (0.8%, 0.6 events per 100 PYE) and placebo (0.5%, 0.3 events per 100 PYE). All were non serious, and the majority were mild in severity. For increased lipase, the proportion of subjects reporting events and event rates were higher for semaglutide 2.4 mg (2.5%, 1.8 events per 100 PYE) compared to placebo (1.3%, 0.9 events per 100 PYE). One (1) SAE, moderate in severity, considered possibly related to trial product and leading to dose interruption was reported. No acute complications, pancreatitis or other pancreas issues were present. The event resolved, with no recurrence reported.

## Supportive studies

In study 4296 , no events related to pancreatitis were reported. Amylase and lipase levels increased from baseline to week 72 in all semaglutide groups. The increase was greater in the semaglutide groups compared to placebo.

## 5.4.4.5. Cardiovascular disorders

There is a strong association between NAFLD/MASH and increased CV risk with CVD being the overall most frequent complication. NAFLD/MASH and CVD share several cardiometabolic risk factors, including obesity, T2D, metabolic syndrome, hypertension, dyslipidaemia, and chronic kidney disease (CKD). The effect of semaglutide 2.4 mg on the risk of MACE was investigated in CVOT EX9536-4388, that included a prespecified analysis of the subpopulation at risk of MASH (see section 5.3.5 Supportive studies). Drugs of the GLP-1 RA class are known to increase pulse rate. In contrast, SBP is decreased by some GLP-1 RA including semaglutide, as observed for semaglutide s.c. for weight management and T2D oral semaglutide for T2D and in subjects with established CVD.

## Study 4553

AEs of cardiovascular disorders were reported by comparable proportions of subjects and event rates with semaglutide 2.4 mg (10.9%, 9.2 events per 100 PYO) compared to placebo (11.4%, 9.0 events per 100 PYO) (Table 40). The majority of the events were non-serious and mild or moderate in severity. Cardiovascular AEs leading to premature treatment discontinuation were reported by 2 subjects in each treatment group. The AEs were distributed across multiple SOCs and PTs, PTs reported by ≥ 1% of subjects are listed in Table 40. The majority of subjects reported the AEs as recovered or not recovered. In total, 3 subjects died of AEs related to cardiovascular disorders, these were all in the placebo group.

SAEs of cardiovascular disorders were reported by comparable proportions of subjects in both treatment groups (semaglutide 2.4 mg: 2.9%; placebo: 2.8%), these SAEs were spread across multiple PTs.

The proportion of subjects reporting events of pre-defined grouped PT increased heart rate were comparable between semaglutide 2.4 mg (0.8%) and placebo (1.3%). All of these events were nonserious, mild or moderate in severity. The majority of events were reported as resolved or not resolved, and none of the events led to a change in trial product.

Cardiovascular disorders based on event adjudication . Events of acute coronary syndrome, cerebrovascular events and heart failure requiring hospitalisation were assessed by an independent EAC. Three (3) deaths were reported as due to AEs of cardiovascular disorders.

Pulse rate . The mean pulse rate at baseline was 75 beats/min in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 74 beats/min in the placebo group. Mean (SD) change from baseline at week 72 was 2 (10) beats/min with semaglutide 2.4 mg and no change for placebo. The proportion of subjects with increase of pulse &gt;= 10 beats/min on at least one occasion was comparable for both treatment arms (n=345; 43.1% vs n=198; 50.1%).

Blood pressure . Blood pressure assessments (SBP and DBP) are evaluated using the FAS (interim). Overall, baseline levels of mean SBP and DBP were within the normal ranges and comparable across treatment groups. Change from baseline to week 72 showed reduction of the (mean) SBP in both treatment groups, with a greater reduction in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group than in the placebo group (-5.39 mmHg vs 1.39 mmHg). No relevant changes were seen for DBP (-1.90 mmHg vs 0.24 mmHg).

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 A total of 4 AEs in 3 subjects (2 subjects in the semaglutide 0.2 mg group and 1 subject in the 0.4 mg group) were classified as cardiovascular events based on event adjudication. Of these, there was 1 event of ischaemic stroke considered non-serious and mild, with the outcome resolved and judged as unlikely related to trial product. Further, 2 events of transient ischemic attack were seen in 1 subject. Of these, 1 was considered mild and 1 moderate and both considered resolved. Further, both events were judged as possibly related to trial product and drug was interrupted. Finally, there was 1 event of sudden cardiac death in the semaglutide 0.2 mg considered unlikely related to trial product. In trial 4296, there were no statistically significant or clinically meaningful changes in pulse rate versus placebo at week 72.

## 5.4.4.6. Neoplasms

Subjects with MASLD/MASH have a higher risk of developing cancer, especially hepatic cancer. The higher risk of cancer seems to be partially linked to the metabolic dysfunction and comorbidities often related to MASH, such as obesity and T2D. To mitigate the risk of carcinomas in the trials, subjects were not eligible for inclusion if they had presence or history within the past 5 years prior to screening of malignant neoplasms other than hepatocellular carcinoma, personal or first-degree relative(s) history of multiple endocrine neoplasia type 2 or medullary thyroid carcinoma (MTC), or presence or history of hepatocellular carcinoma at randomisation (only trials 4553 and 4492).

## Study 4553

In trial 4553 (interim evaluation), AEs of neoplasms (benign and malignant) were reported by comparable proportions of subjects and event rates with semaglutide 2.4 mg (8.5%, 6.3 events per 100 PYO) compared to placebo (9.9%, 8.4 events per 100 PYO). The majority of events were nonserious, mild in severity and unlikely related to trial product. Two (2) events in 2 subjects in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 3 events in 3 subjects in the placebo group led to premature trial product discontinuation.

The most frequently reported PTs were renal cyst, large intestine polyp and colorectal adenoma. Renal cysts were reported by more subjects in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group (1.6%) compared to placebo (0.5%). The majority of subjects reporting renal cysts in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group co-reported gastrointestinal AEs or other AEs (e.g. musculoskeletal disorders) that could lead to imaging and thereby incidental findings of renal cysts. The remaining AEs were distributed across multiple PTs with few events reported for each PT and with no notable pattern with respect to organ system of origin or distribution between the treatment groups.

The proportions of subjects with SAEs were comparable with semaglutide 2.4 mg (2.3%) and placebo (2.8%). The SAEs were distributed across multiple PTs with few events (1-3) reported for each PT. Of the subjects with SAEs, 3 subjects (1 in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 2 in the placebo group) had events with fatal outcome.

Malignant neoplasms based on AEs. AEs of malignant neoplasms were reported by comparable proportions of subjects and event rates with semaglutide 2.4 mg (1.8%, 1.2 events per 100 PYO) compared to placebo (2.5%, 2.1 events per 100 PYO). The majority of events were severe and/or serious. In each group, 1 event was considered possibly related to trial product. The remaining events were unlikely related to trial product. Two (2) events in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 1 event in the placebo group led to premature trial product discontinuation. Overall, AEs were distributed across multiple PTs with few events (1-2) reported for each PT. Approximately 1/3 of the events reported were different PTs of skin neoplasms (4 events in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group versus 7 events in the

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

placebo group). The remaining events showed no clustering of specific PTs. One (1) subject in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 2 subjects in the placebo group had events with fatal outcomes.

## Supportive studies

In trial 4296 (dosing: 0.1 mg/day, 0.2 mg/day or 0.4 mg/day in 80, 78 and 81 subjects, respectively) neoplasms formed in 12.5%; 14.1% and 17.5 % of subjects, respectively. In the placebo group (80 subjects) neoplasms formed in 7.5 % of subjects. Gastrointestinal (sema 0.1mg: 1 subject (1.3%), sema 0.2 mg: 4 subjects (5.1%), sema 0.4 mg: 5 subjects (6.2%) vs placebo: 0) and hepatobiliary neoplasms (sema 0.1mg: 0, sema 0.2 mg: 1 subjects (1.3%), sema 0.4 mg: 2 subjects (2.5%) vs placebo: 0) were reported at higher frequency at higher semaglutide dose. Renal cysts don't show dose-dependency (sema 0.1mg: 3 subject (3.8%), sema 0.2 mg: 1 subject (1.3%), sema 0.4 mg: 0, placebo: 1 (1.3%).

## 5.4.4.7. Acute renal failure

Gastrointestinal side effects associated with GLP-1 RA may cause dehydration, which in rare cases can lead to a deterioration of renal function. MASH and obesity are linked to an increased risk of developing chronic kidney disease (CKD), which could cause increased vulnerability in case of dehydration. To mitigate the risk of acute renal failure, subjects were not eligible for inclusion in any of the trials if they had eGFR &lt; 30 ml/min/1.73 m 2 .

## Study 4553

AEs of acute renal failure were reported by comparable proportions of subjects and event rates with semaglutide 2.4 mg (0.6%, 0.7 events per 100 PYE) compared to placebo (0.5%, 0.3 events per 100 PYE). The majority of AEs related to acute renal failure were non-serious, mild or moderate in severity and unlikely related to trial product. More than half of the events resolved. One (1) subject had 1 event leading to premature trial product discontinuation. AEs were distributed across the PTs acute kidney injury, renal failure, azotaemia, renal impairment. With 4 events reported by 3 subjects in the semaglutide 2.4 mg group and 1 event reported by 1 subject in the placebo group, acute kidney injury was the most frequently reported PT.

Two (2) subjects, reported a total of 3 SAEs (azotaemia, acute kidney injury and renal failure). One (1) event led to premature trial product discontinuation and 2 events to temporary discontinuation.

eGFR and creatinine . Mean eGFR values decreased slightly during the first 12 weeks. At week 72 (interim), there was no change compared to baseline. There was no difference in mean eGFR values for semaglutide 2.4 mg compared to placebo (Figure 19). Mean creatinine values increased slightly for semaglutide 2.4 mg during the first 12 weeks, after which values stabilised and then slowly decreased towards baseline values. At week 72 (interim), there was no change compared to baseline and no difference compared to placebo. No change in creatinine values was seen for placebo.

## Supportive studies

Study 4296 Within the SOC Renal and urinary disorders, a total of 6 events with PTs renal impairment, acute kidney injury or renal failure were identified, 4 (1.7%) events in subjects on semaglutide (n=1, n=2, and n=1 on semaglutide 0.1 mg, 0.2 mg and 0.4 mg OD) and 2 (2.5%) events on placebo. Two (2) events of acute kidney injury, both in the semaglutide 0.2 mg group, were considered SAEs and led to temporary discontinuation of trial product. In addition, one of these events were considered severe. All other events were mild or moderate in severity.

## 5.4.4.8. Hypoglycaemia

During conduct of trial 4553, non-serious events of hypoglycaemia occurring in subjects with T2D, were not to be recorded as AEs, but using the hypoglycaemic-episodes form only, whereas serious episodes were to be reported as SAEs. For subjects without T2D, blood glucose was not monitored, any events of hypoglycaemia were to be reported as AEs only. For trial 4553, hypoglycaemic episodes reported by subjects with T2D are categorised as level 1-3 according to the ADA 2023 classification (Table 41). For subjects without T2D, AEs of hypoglycaemia are evaluated based on a predefined MedDRA search.

Table 39: Classification of hypoglycaemia - subjects with T2D - trial 4553

| Level                                          | Glycaemic criteria                                | Description                                                                                                                           |
|------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Hypoglycaemia alert value (level 1)            | <3.9 mmol/L (70 mg/dL) and ≥3.0 mmol/L (54 mg/dL) | Sufficiently low for treatment with fast-acting carbohydrate and dose adjustment of glucose- lowering therapy                         |
| Clinically significant hypoglycaemia (level 2) | <3.0 mmol/L (54 mg/dL)                            | Sufficiently low to indicate serious, clinically important hypoglycaemia                                                              |
| Severe hypoglycaemia (level 3)                 | No specific glucose threshold                     | A severe event characterised by altered mental and/or physical functioning that requires assistance from another person for recovery. |

T2D: type 2 diabetes.

In trial 4296, hypoglycaemic episodes reported by subjects with T2D are evaluated using the ADA 2013 classification and further evaluated as 'severe or blood glucose (BG) confirmed symptomatic hypoglycaemia' based on the Novo Nordisk classification (Table 40).

Table 40: NN classification of hypoglycaemia - subjects with T2D - trial 4296

| Classification                                    | Glycaemic criteria                                                                                                                                         |
|---------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Severe or BG confirmed symptomatic hypoglycaemia: | Severe according to the ADA classification a or BG confirmed by a plasma glucose value <3.1 mmol/L (56 mg/dL) with symptoms, consistent with hypoglycaemia |

## Study 4553

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

The proportion of subjects with T2D at baseline reporting hypoglycaemic episodes was higher with semaglutide 2.4 mg (19.3%, 39.6 events per 100 PYE) compared to placebo (13.1%, 51.3 events per 100 PYE) whereas event rates were higher in the placebo group (Table 41). In both groups a few subjects reported multiple events, which impacted the event rates.
