AEs for which a causal relation with semaglutide was judged by the investigator as at least a reasonable possibility, are proposed to be included in section 4.8 of the SmPC as Adverse Drug Reactions. The majority of ADRs included in the SmPC 4.8 ADR table are in accordance with the information on related AEs as presented in the CSR of ESSENCE study. For the events of myalgia and muscle spasms, depression and depressed mood, and diverticulitis minor increases are observed in the semaglutide group, although the differences are small and most cases were considered unlikely to be related to the drug. No updates of the SmPC were considered necessary.

In addition to AEs reported in pivotal study 4553 (ESSENCE) in the target population at the target dose of 2.4 mg once weekly that are causally related to semaglutide, also ADRs reported in studies on Wegovy in weight management are included in the listing of adverse events.

## 5.4.12.2. Conclusions on clinical safety

Based on the currently available safety data in patients with MASH F2/F3 treated for at least 72 weeks, semaglutide appears to be acceptably tolerated, with 82% of subjects uptitrated to the target dose of 2.4 mg once weekly, and only 3.3% discontinuing treatment due to AEs. Gastrointestinal AEs were the most common AEs reported, predominantly nausea, diarrhoea, vomiting and constipation, mainly occurring during dose escalation phase, though nausea was reported throughout treatment. SAEs were reported in a limited number of cases, without clustering of specific events, leading only to discontinuation of semaglutide in 0.3% of subjects. No differences in safety profile were seen across stages of MASH, or presence of concomitant T2D, and in general the safety profile was consistent with semaglutide in T2D and for weight management.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 6. Risk management plan

## 6.1. Safety specification

## 6.1.1. Proposed safety specification

The applicant proposed the following summary of safety concerns in the RMP:

Table 44: Summary of safety concerns in the proposed RMP

| Summary of safety concerns   | Summary of safety concerns                                                                       |
|------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Important identified risks   | • Diabetic retinopathy complications (only for patients with T2D)                                |
| Important potential risks    | • Pancreatic cancer • Medullary thyroid cancer                                                   |
| Missing information          | • Pregnancy • Breastfeeding • Patients with severe hepatic impairment • Patients with lean MASH* |

## 6.1.2. Discussion on proposed safety specification

Extensive data from clinical development programs as well as post-marketing data are available on semaglutide in T2D and in weight management. The RMP for Kayshild is overall in line with the RMP of previous semaglutide products.

Nevertheless, for Kayshild 'patients with lean MASH' is proposed as missing information in the RMP. The number of subjects included in study 4553 with lean MASH (MASH and BMI &lt; 25 kg/m2 (or BMI &lt; 23 kg/m2 for Asian population) is very limited (N=76; n=52 in semaglutide and n=24 in placebo) and the current indication is the first indication for semaglutide that includes patients with BMI&lt;27. Further, interruption or reduction of semaglutide dose was reported more frequently in subjects with BMI &lt; 27 kg/m2 vs BMI&gt;27kg/m2, in 21.2% vs 8.0%-13.7% and 21.2% vs 5.9%-12.2%, respectively, pointing to potential tolerance issues of semaglutide in this population. Therefore, inclusion in the listing of Missing information was accepted, and the limited information in lean MASH patients was appropriately reflected in section 4.4 of the SmPC.

## 6.2. Pharmacovigilance plan

## 6.2.1. Proposed pharmacovigilance plan

## Routine Pharmacovigilance activities

No routine pharmacovigilance activities beyond adverse reactions reporting/ PSURs and signal detection are deemed necessary to monitor the risks related to semaglutide.

## 6.2.2. Discussion on the pharmacovigilance plan

The routine pharmacovigilance activities proposed by the applicant are considered acceptable.

Additional pharmacovigilance activities include on-going post-authorisation safety studies (PASSs) regarding the important identified risk of diabetic retinopathy complications, the important potential risks of medullary thyroid cancer (MTC) and pancreatic cancer. The MASH patients were suggested to be included in the PASS for MTC, which was agreed. Information was added for the PASSs of diabetic retinopathy complications and pancreatic cancer that the results of these PASSs would also be relevant for the on-going evaluation of the risk for semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg for MASH. The additional pharmacovigilance activities proposed above are acceptable.

## 7. Pharmacovigilance

## 7.1. Pharmacovigilance system

The CHMP rapporteur considers that the pharmacovigilance system summary submitted by the applicant fulfils the requirements of Article 8(3) of Directive 2001/83/EC.

## 7.2. Periodic safety update reports (PSURs) submission requirements

Since this is an application for a conditional marketing authorisation (CMA) in accordance with Article 14-a of Regulation (EC) No 726/2004, the PRAC rapporteur is of the opinion that a separate entry in the list of Union reference dates (EURD list) for Kayshild is needed, as it cannot follow the already existing entry for semaglutide. The requirements for submission of periodic safety update reports for this medicinal product are set out in the Annex II, Section C of the CHMP Opinion. The PSUR cycle for Kayshild should follow a half-yearly cycle. The data lock point (DLP) of the new EURD list entry for Kayshild should be aligned with the DLP of the existing semaglutide entry, facilitating for a fusion of the two if desired in the future.

## 8. Product information

## 8.1. Summary of Product Characteristics (SmPC)

## 8.1.1. SmPC section 4.1 justification

The proposed indication is aligned with the population studied in the pivotal study.

## 8.1.2. SmPC section 5.1 justification

Information on the pivotal study supporting the indication is included in the SmPC section 5.1.

Besides key findings under alpha spending control, some additional secondary endpoints have been included which are considered of clinical relevance to the prescriber comparable to other approved medicinal products for MASH.

## 8.2. Labelling

## 8.2.1. User consultation

## 8.2.1.1. Conclusion from the checklist for the review of user consultation

A justification for not performing a full user consultation with target patient groups on the package leaflet has been submitted by the applicant and has been found acceptable for the following reasons:

No full user consultation with target patient groups on the package leaflet has been performed on the basis of a bridging report making reference to Rybelsus and Wegovy. The bridging report submitted by the applicant has been found acceptable.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 8.2.2. Labelling exemptions

A request to omit certain particulars from the labelling as per Art.63.1 of Directive 2001/83/EC has been submitted by the applicant and has been found acceptable by the QRD Group. In the 113 th  QRD meeting (June 2025) it was accepted to use mg per dose, instead of the QRD reference for the expression of strength for parenteral in multidose containers (mg/mL).

## 8.3. Additional monitoring

Pursuant to Article 23(1) of Regulation No (EU) 726/2004, Kayshild ([semaglutide]) is included in the additional monitoring list since it contains a new active substance which, on 1 January 2011, was not contained in any medicinal product authorised in the EU;

Therefore, the summary of product characteristics and the package leaflet includes a statement that this medicinal product is subject to additional monitoring and will allow quick identification of new safety information. The statement is preceded by an inverted equilateral black triangle.&gt;

## 9. Benefit-risk assessment

## 9.1. Therapeutic context

## 9.1.1. Disease or condition, proposed therapeutic indication

Metabolic dysfunction associated steatohepatitis (MASH) is a progressive liver disease, part of the spectrum of metabolic associated fatty liver diseases (MAFLD). It is estimated that the global prevalence of NAFLD is approximately 30% and increasing, and the global prevalence of MASH in the general population is estimated to be between 4% and 14%.

In approximately 20% of people with NAFLD, fatty liver disease progresses to MASH. As MASH progresses, fibrosis can lead to cirrhosis, associated with further complications such as hepatic decompensation events, liver failure and hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC), and increased risk for cardiovascular disease and (CV) mortality. NAFLD/MASH and cardiovascular disease share several cardiometabolic risk factors, including obesity, T2D, metabolic syndrome, hypertension, dyslipidaemia, and chronic kidney disease (CKD). Further, the presence of obesity and T2D increases the risk of fibrosis progression in MASH. Around 34% of people with obesity are believed to have MASH. Amongst people with T2D, global data indicate that around 66% have MASH, with 41% having significant liver fibrosis.

NAFLD and MASH are multifactorial diseases. Contributing factors include dysregulation of the lipogenic pathway, oxidative stress, genetic predisposition, altered immune responses, and gut microbiome dysbiosis. There is a growing body of evidence linking NAFLD and MASH pathogenesis with mechanisms of metabolic dysfunction, through liver lipid accumulation, insulin resistance, inflammation, apoptosis, and liver fibrosis.

The applicant proposed the following indication:

Kayshild is indicated in conjunction with diet and exercise for the treatment of adults with non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunction-associated steatohepatitis (MASH) with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (fibrosis stages F2 to F3).

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 9.1.2. Available therapies and unmet medical need

For a detailed description, please see section 2.1 of this document.

Liver fibrosis may be reversible, the evolution of MASH can be bidirectional, and the progression of MASH could potentially be stabilised or even reversed. The Reflection paper on regulatory requirements for the development of medicinal products for non-alcoholic steatohepatitis (NASH) (EMA/CHMP/111529/2024) acknowledge the unmet medical need.

Lifestyle changes, including diet and exercise have been considered standard of care. Treatments used off-label for the treatment MASH include Vitamin E, pioglitazone and GLP-1 Ras, which have been recommended by learned societies.

Recently, a medicinal product for MASH (Rezdiffra, INN: resmetirom) was granted a conditional marketing authorisation (Commission Decision issued on 18 August 2025).

Obesity and diabetes are risk factors for MASH, and a considerable proportion of the MASH population are obese patients and/or T2DM patients. Semaglutide is indicated to treat overweight patients (a BMI of 30 kg/m² or greater (obesity) or a BMI of at least 27 kg/m² but less than 30 kg/m² (overweight) who have weight-related health problems (such as diabetes, high blood pressure, dyslipidemia), or for the treatment of T2DM.

Bariatric surgery may be optional, however, is an invasive procedure that remains associated with several major risks, including surgical complications.

## 9.2. Main clinical studies

For a detailed description of the main clinical studies supporting this application, please refer to section 5.3.2 of this document.

The pivotal phase 3 study was a randomised, multicentre, double-blind, parallel-group phase 3 design to compare semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg once weekly versus placebo s.c. once weekly (on top of standard of care) in 800 subjects (2:1) with MASH and F2 or F3 (recruitment cap of approximately 20% for subjects with F2), with a 16-week dose escalation phase, to demonstrate at the interim analyses that treatment with semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg improves liver histology as based on the co-primary endpoints of Resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis , and Improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis, at Week 72. The (alpha controlled) key secondary endpoints included Resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis, Reduction in body weight, and Change in SF-36 Bodily Pain. The study included patients with confirmed stage F2 or F3 (with biopsy within 180 days), and a NAS ≥ 4 with a score of 1 or more in steatosis, lobular inflammation and hepatocyte ballooning, as based on a central pathologist evaluation. Both existing marketed single and multiple injectors (and placebo paired injectors) were used. A data monitoring committee independently and adjudicated events in a blinded manner.

The objective of Part 2 of the study is to demonstrate that treatment with semaglutide s.c. 2.4 mg lowers the risk of liver-related clinical events compared to placebo in subjects with MASH and fibrosis stage 2 or 3 at latest of 240 weeks.

## 9.3. Favourable effects

Primary endpoints Semaglutide was superior to placebo on intermediate histological endpoints at the pre-planned Week 72 interim of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis (62.9% vs 34.4%; 28.65 %-points [21.09; 36.21]95% CI; p-value &lt;0.0001), and improvement in liver fibrosis

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

and no worsening of steatohepatitis (36.8% vs 22.4%; 14.39 %-points [7.51; 21.27]95% CI; p-value &lt;0.0001). Sensitivity analyses were in agreement with these main findings.

Subgroup analyses The results were consistent across important subgroups of both endpoints. Especially, consistent findings were observed for the F2 and F3 subgroups, and for all subgroup categories of BMI also including &lt;25 kg/m2 and 25-30 kg/m2 patients. Weight lowering in relation to MASH for patients at the lower weight/BMI spectrum was also achieved, and some limited data suggest that the greatest reduction was achieved on fat mass instead of lean body mass (STEP 12 in China/Asia).

Key secondary endpoints (under alpha control) Hierarchical testing demonstrated statistical significant effect of semaglutide on secondary endpoints of change in body weight (-10.51 kg for semaglutide vs -2.04 kg for placebo; -8.46 %-points [ -9.55; -7.38]95%CI; p-value &lt; 0.0001), and resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis (32.7% vs 16.1%; 16.54% [ 10.24; 22.83]95%CI; p-value &lt;0.0001).

Other secondary (and exploratory) liver related endpoints Numerical statistical improvements could be observed for other (exploratory) secondary endpoints of histological MASH/liver related endpoints, liver-related imaging-based endpoints (FibroScan), and numerical statistical improvements in liver enzymes including alanine aminotransferase (ALT) and aspartate aminotransferase (AST), and other blood fibrosis biomarkers (Pro-C3 score and Enhanced Liver Fibrosis score).

Other secondary (and exploratory) cardiometabolic endpoints Numerical improvements were generally observed in other cardiometabolic markers (diabetes markers (HbA1c, HOMA-IR (exploratory)) (both diabetic and non-diabetic), lipid markers, and inflammation markers (hsCRP (secondary), TNF-alpha and IL-1R antagonist (exploratory)).

## 9.3.1. Uncertainties and limitations about favourable effects

Patient reported outcomes A clear effect on patient reported outcomes could not be demonstrated. The fourth hierarchical tested endpoint of patient reported outcome of SF-36 Bodily pain was not significant (0.86 vs -0.47; 1.34 [ 0.01; 2.67]95% CI; p-value =0.0488). Numerical improvement could be observed for the SF-36 Physical Component, SF-36 Mental Component, but not for MASHCHECK abdominal pain. The general nature of the instrument of Change in SF-36 Bodily Pain does not entirely discriminate whether the changes in score from baseline to 72 weeks may be due to an effect of MASH or due to other related factors, such as reduction in BMI.

Mechanism of action The mechanism of action remains not entirely elucidated. Numerical improvements in cardiometabolic markers of weight reduction, diabetes markers (HbA1c, HOMA-IR (exploratory)) (both diabetic and non-diabetic), lipid markers, and inflammation markers (hsCRP, TNF-alpha and IL-1R antagonist) across the studies, may only constitute an indirect benefit. Nonclinical models could identify 72 proteins could be associated with the resolution of MASH, of which 26 may not be associated to weight loss, rather potentially to fibrosis and inflammation or other mechanism that have not been elucidated. These could also be associated with a proteomic phenotype in the phase 2 study and could possibly also be verified once the phase 3 study has been completed. Nevertheless, based on post hoc analyses, a relevant proportion of the treatment effects appears independent of HbA1c control and body weight reduction.

Clinical endpoints and long-term efficacy As per the current interim results, no treatment effect has been demonstrated on clinical endpoints. Such evidence is expected at the end of the on-going phase 3 study. Nevertheless, once a positive opinion would be disseminated, this could raise a risk to the study integrity, e.g. causing additional drop-outs. The measures proposed by the Applicant in this

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

respect, as described further in the discussion on CMA below, were considered sufficient.

Age A consistent effect for patients over 65 years of age has been demonstrated for the primary endpoints, however, data on older age categories are limited. Only 20 patients were included in the study for the 75-85 age subgroup and none above 85 years of age. However, there appears to be comparable PK, and efficacy across subgroups of more or less than 70 years of age.

## 9.4. Unfavourable effects

Exposure In the pivotal study 4553, a total of 800 subjects with the indication of MASH F2-F3 were exposed to semaglutide targeted at a dose of 2.4 mg once weekly, with a total of 542 subjects treated for at least 12 months. The target dose of 2.4 mg was reached by 81.7% subjects treated with semaglutide at week 24.

Adverse events were reported at higher frequency in subjects on semaglutide as compared with placebo (86.3% vs 78.7%), predominantly gastrointestinal AEs (69.5% versus 46.8%), and were deemed probably or possibly related to the study drug in 68.6% vs 40.8%. Serious AEs were reported at comparable frequency on semaglutide (13.0%) vs placebo (12.9%).

Gastro-intestinal adverse events . Main adverse events reported concern gastro-intestinal adverse events, in 69.5% of subjects on semaglutide as compared with 46.8% of subjects on placebo, mainly nausea (36.1% vs 12.4%), diarrhoea (26.8% vs 12.2%), constipation (22.1% vs 7.8%) and vomiting (18.5% vs 5.6%). Decreased appetite was reported by 14.0% vs 2.5% of subjects.

Gallbladder related disorders were reported at slightly increased frequency on semaglutide (2.5% vs 1.5% of subjects), most frequently concerning cholelithiasis (1.4% vs 0.8%). Symptomatic acute gallbladder disease was seen at slightly increased frequency on semaglutide, in 5 vs 2 subjects.

Acute pancreatitis . A total of 5 events of acute pancreatitis were reported, 3 (0.4%) on semaglutide and 2 (0.5%) on placebo. Out of these, 3 events were categorised as SAE, 2 (0.3%) vs 1 (0.3%).

Hypoglycaemic events . In subjects with T2D at baseline, hypoglycaemic events were reported more frequently in the semaglutide group, 19.3% vs 13.1% on placebo. Also, serious, clinically important hypoglycaemia (level 2, &lt;3.0 mmol/l) and severe hypoglycaemia (requiring assistance from another person) were reported more frequently on semaglutide, in 6.1% vs 5.0% and 2.2% vs 0.5% of subjects, respectively.

## Safety profile across subgroups.

- Across MASH stage F1-F4c no difference in safety profile was seen.
- In subjects with baseline BMI&lt; 27 kg/m2, interruption or reduction of semaglutide dose was reported more frequently than in higher BMI categories, in 21.2% vs 8.0%-13.7% and 21.2% vs 5.9%-12.2% of subjects, respectively.
- A higher proportion of subjects &gt;= 65 years of age on semaglutide reported SAEs, in 14.8% at age &gt;=65 years vs 10.8% &lt; 45 years, and severe AEs (11.9% vs 5.0%).
- In female subjects in the semaglutide group, SAEs were reported more frequently than in male subjects, in 15.5% vs 9.7%.

## 9.4.1. Uncertainties and limitations about unfavourable effects

The duration of exposure to semaglutide 2.4 mg in the target population with MASH F2-F3, of 87.1 (50.7) weeks on semaglutide, and 82.8 (49.9) weeks on placebo is still limited, especially for assessing less frequently occurring adverse events that may occur at increasing frequency during

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

prolonged treatment, like cholelithiasis, acute pancreatitis, or neoplasms. This is accepted in the context of a CMA.

Temporary discontinuation or dose reduction of semaglutide were reported at increased frequency as compared with placebo, in 12% vs 6.8% and 10.0% vs 2.0%, respectively. Premature discontinuation of study treatment was only required in a small proportion of subjects without imbalance between study-arms (3.3% vs 2.6%).

There was a not-negligible chance of unblinding due to the characteristic and very common gastrointestinal AEs of semaglutide, and this effect in principle might hamper the assessment of clinical safety. Still, the safety profile of semaglutide in the general population is well established.

Higher rates of severe hypoglycaemic events were reported during the trial compared to previous studies with semaglutide. No new factors with a correlation to hypoglycaemic events have been identified. Additionally, the classification for severe hypoglycaemia in study 4553 did not include a specific glucose level threshold, but a description including an event with altered mental state and need of support from another person. Out of the 12 severe events, for half of the events plasmaglucose values were &gt;3.0 mmol/L (54 mg/dL), and 10 were treated and resolved with water and food. This indicates that these events could have been classified as clinically relevant, rather than severe. In such case, the rates of severe events are considered less remarkable, and overall in line with other trials with semaglutide (e.g., STEP2).In study 4553, in subjects without T2DM at baseline AEs of hypoglycaemia were evaluated based on a predefined MedDRA search only, as opposed to recording using a specific hypoglycaemic-episode form in patients with T2D, and therefore may be at risk of underreporting. Additionally, a higher proportion of subjects without T2D reported potentially hypoglycaemia-related AEs in the semaglutide group (7.1 %) compared to placebo (5.8 %), however there is no clear additional risk for hypoglycaemia in NT2DM.

Safety data in patients &gt;=75 years are very limited or not available. There is uncertainty about the safety risks in elderly subjects . The limited information available was reflected in the SmPC.

There is uncertainty about a potentially increased frequency of renal cysts (in 1.6% of subjects on semaglutide vs 0.5% on placebo), although none of the cysts showed malignancy and it is plausible that the higher number of events are due to chance finding when evaluating other AEs (primarily GI AEs).

In trial 4296 dose dependence of AE frequencies in Neoplasm SOC was observed with the highest AE frequency of 17.5% in the 0.4 mg/day dose group (vs 7.5% in placebo group). In Study 4553, however, the frequency of neoplasm AEs was roughly half compared to the previous study and in similar proportion compared to placebo (8.5% in semaglutide 2.4 mg/week vs 9.9% in placebo group).

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 9.6. Benefit-risk assessment and discussion

## 9.6.1. Importance of favourable and unfavourable effects

Semaglutide has demonstrated a significant treatment effect on both the histological endpoints of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis with a 29% difference (62.9% vs 34.4%) and 14% improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis (36.8% vs 22.4%) in a reasonable time period of 72 weeks to expect a treatment effect. Histological evaluation of liver biopsies is currently considered the golden standard in the clinical trials for diagnosis and for followup of the disease, despite sampling error and possible evaluation variability. Still, histological endpoints have not been validated as true surrogates in absence of sufficient predictive data to quantitatively relate a treatment response to clinical improvement in the long-term. Nevertheless, histological intermediate endpoints are chosen as they reasonably predict the long-term outcome, and with independent statistical significance on both endpoints this is thought to account for uncertainties as much as possible in relation to possible clinical outcomes, as mentioned in the EMA MASH guideline. However, longer term data is needed to demonstrate that these intermediate benefits will also translate into clinical improvement.

Support has been provided by a significant improvement on the key secondary endpoint of resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis. However, this endpoint may highly overlap with the resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis endpoint, and thus may have limited independent value, nevertheless increasing robustness of the combined data.

The demonstrated reduction in weight of -8.5% (10.5-2), comparable to what is seen in other indications, may indirectly support to some extent the benefits in MASH, as there appears an association between both. The exact mechanism has not been entirely elucidated, and other effects likely contribute to the treatment effect. Also, in the small subgroup of patients with BMI between 25 to 30 beneficial effects on the primary evaluation were demonstrated, which also could to some part be associated with weight reduction.

Results on patient reported outcomes were not that clear, with no clear beneficial treatment effects across the different questionnaire instruments. Also, it is questioned whether the key instrument of SF-36 Bodily Pain is able to specifically discriminate effects on MASH associated symptoms, especially in a non-cirrhotic population. The relevance of such findings is further complicated by symptoms possibly resulting from (other) co-morbidities in such a population. And although patients' well-being is important, given these uncertainties, such evaluation may thus be of limited value.

In general, the safety profile of semaglutide 2.4 mg once weekly in MASH F2-F3 is in line with findings from semaglutide in T2D and in weight management. Gastro-intestinal AEs of nausea, vomiting, diarrhoea and constipation occur frequently, mainly in the initial uptitration phase, and in general can be managed by (temporal) dose adaptation. Permanent discontinuation is only required in a small proportion of subjects. However, adverse events of cholelithiasis and acute pancreatitis, though occurring at low frequency, may have an unfavourable course in MASH patients, although current data do not show clear causality. Also, frequency of hypoglycaemia is higher than reported on other semaglutide trials, although comparable to trials such as STEP2. Long-term safety data in the MASH population are lacking, which may impact estimation of potential persistent or long-term safety risks, beyond what is known from experience with existing semaglutide indications.

## 9.6.2. Balance of benefits and risks

In general, semaglutide has demonstrated a beneficial effect by a significant improvement in both

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

intermediate relevant histological endpoints of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis and improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis during an intermediate time frame of 72 weeks, which are thought to be reasonably likely to predict clinical outcome in the long term. Some supportive evidence on a beneficial effect come from an already known effect on body weight lowering, and a supportive histological endpoint of resolution of steatohepatitis and improvement in liver fibrosis. A series of other less relevant secondary endpoints of liver-related markers and cardiometabolic markers show numerical improvements, which may provide some further confidence on the observed treatment effect.

Nevertheless, whether these observed treatment effects will translate into long-term benefit remains to be seen and should be demonstrated by the on-going pivotal study.

The safety profile of semaglutide has already been largely characterised by evidence and experience in other approved indications. Semaglutide demonstrates a comparable safety profile in the current MASH population. Long-term safety data in the MASH population are lacking, which may impact estimation of potential persistent or long-term safety. Apart from these uncertainties, the safety profile could be considered acceptable.

Overall, semaglutide demonstrates a positive benefit risk based on interim results in a population of F2 or F3 fibrosis MASH.

## 9.6.3. Additional considerations on the benefit-risk balance

## 9.6.3.1. Conditional marketing authorisation

## 9.6.3.1.1. Applicant's request for Conditional marketing authorisation

The applicant requested in the initial submission consideration of its application for a Conditional marketing authorisation in accordance with Article 14-a of Regulation (EC) No 726/2004, based on the following criteria:

- The benefit-risk balance is positive in the following indication Kayshild is indicated in conjunction with diet and exercise for the treatment of non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunctionassociated steatohepatitis (MASH) with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (fibrosis stages F2 to F3)

The applicant has stated that the balance between the benefits and the risks identified for semaglutide 2.4 mg for the treatment of non-cirrhotic MASH with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis is considered favourable with the benefits outweighing the risks. In their view, the clinical development programme confirmed that semaglutide 2.4 mg led to clinically meaningful improvements in liver histology and other liver-related parameters, as well as to body weight loss and other cardiometabolic benefits. In addition, results confirmed that semaglutide 2.4 mg reduces the risk of MACE in people at risk of MASH. The safety and tolerability profiles were in line with those of semaglutide 2.4 mg for weight management (Wegovy) and of the GLP-1 RA drug class in general. The applicant has added that it is likely they will be able to provide comprehensive data.

The CMA application of semaglutide 2.4 mg for MASH is based primarily on an interim evaluation of trial 4553 (part 1) and the completed trial 4296. The primary endpoints of part 1 of trial 4553 as well as trial 4296 are intermediate liver histology endpoints, which according to the available regulatory guidelines and as supported by retrospective and prospective data are likely to predict a clinical benefit. The trial design is compliant with the EMA's reflection paper and has been discussed with EMA

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

in a scientific advice procedure.

To confirm that the documented improvements in liver histology with semaglutide 2.4 mg lead to meaningful benefits in clinically relevant liver-related outcomes, such as hepatic decompensation or progression to cirrhosis, the applicant has confirmed that part 2 of trial 4553 will continue in a blinded manner and be conducted with due diligence. Part 2 of trial 4553 also serves to assess long-term safety in patients with MASH. The primary endpoint for part 2 is a composite endpoint, which is prespecified as cirrhosis-free survival at week 240 (cirrhosis-free survival corresponds to not having experienced one of the following types of liver-related clinical events: histological progression to cirrhosis, all-cause mortality, liver-induced model for end-stage liver disease (MELD) score ≥15, liver transplant or hepatic decompensation events.). Results from part 2 are anticipated to be available in 2029.

In order to ensure that Novo Nordisk will be able to provide comprehensive data, trial 4553 must remain double-blind after the interim evaluation (i.e., through mid-2029) and retention of the trial participants is crucial to ensure sufficient trial power.

Trial 4553 has completed global recruitment and a total of 1197 participants were randomised to trial products. The last patient, last visit (LPLV) is planned for April 2029. Novo Nordisk added that the company understands the importance of retaining participants in trial 4553 and has focused efforts to maximise retention.

Accordingly, Novo Nordisk has pre-emptively worked to ensure that initiatives to ensure adequate retention have been implemented during part 1 of the trial and that additional initiatives have been developed for part 2 of the trial. For example, trends in general retention, withdrawal and lost-tofollow-up, including patterns in the specific reasons, are closely monitored by trial management on an ongoing basis. Other important aspects of mitigatory actions include proactive identification and followup with participants at risk of withdrawing, close contact with the trial investigators and site staff as well as regular meetings with national lead principal investigators from all countries. Targeted participant and site material is available, including guidance on putting the part 1 results of trial 4553 in context. The current annual withdrawal rate in trial 4553 is 2.7%, which is in line with expectations. If needed, increased focus will be implemented, such as additional advising, education or retraining of site staff, development of new tools or revision of current tools and materials for retention.

The applicant motivated the choice of placebo as comparator, due to lack of pharmacological treatment options for patients with MASH. Furthermore, investigators were encouraged to provide standard of care in MASH. The company has added that, should a pharmacological treatment for MASH be approved during the conduct of this trial, the participants will also be able to initiate this treatment during part 2 after completing visit 13 (week 72) while continuing in the trial. This is in accordance with a pragmatic approach to compare two treatment regimens: one where semaglutide is available and another where it is not.

Additionally, protection of sensitive data by limiting public dissemination of such data until after the end of part 2 of trial 4553 is an important aspect to maintain trial integrity and minimise the impact on trial conduct and retention. Novo Nordisk has taken pre-emptive action to ensure that trial integritypreserving procedures are pre-specified in an 'Interim Evaluation Charter' (Interim evaluation charter for trial NN9931-4553 (M5.3.5.1)). It is acknowledged that it is crucial for the generation of comprehensive data that the integrity of the post-interim part of trial 4553 is not compromised by the interim evaluation, for example as a result of introduction of biases due to the disclosure of specific informationor unintentional unblinding of the trial until the end of part 2.

Based on experience from other large, long-term Novo Nordisk outcomes trials (e.g. the ongoing post-

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

authorisation safety trial FOCUS [NN9535-4352] and the completed CVOT SELECT), Novo Nordisk remains confident that comprehensive data can be provided at end of part 2 of trial 4553 to confirm the meaningful benefits on clinically relevant liver-related outcomes in patients with MASH.

## · Unmet medical needs will be addressed, as

MASH is a serious progressive liver disease, which is part of the spectrum of metabolic dysfunctionassociated steatotic liver disease (MASLD). The incidence of MASH is rising globally and may be underestimated due to a lack of awareness of MASH and missed diagnosis. It is estimated that the global prevalence of MASLD is approximately 30% and increasing. The global prevalence of MASH in the general population is estimated to be between 4% and 7%, based on data from 20194.

In approximately 20% of people with MASLD, steatotic liver disease progresses to MASH5, which is characterised by the presence of hepatic steatosis in at least 5% of hepatic cells with inflammation and hepatocyte injury (also known as hepatocyte ballooning), with or without evidence of liver fibrosis. As MASH progresses, fibrosis can lead to cirrhosis, which is associated with further complications such as hepatic decompensation events, liver failure and hepatocellular carcinoma. Consequently, MASH is one of the main indications for liver transplantation in many countries. The risk of mortality in MASLD/MASH increases with disease severity, with cardiovascular disease being the most common cause of death in people with MASLD. MASH progression is associated with increased risk of complications. In people with MASH and advanced fibrosis, liver-related events are the most frequent complication. A strong association between MASLD/MASH and increased cardiovascular risk is recognised with cardiovascular disease being the overall most frequent complication. MASLD/MASH and cardiovascular disease share several cardiometabolic risk factors, including obesity, T2D, metabolic syndrome, hypertension, dyslipidaemia, and chronic kidney disease.

MASLD and MASH are closely associated with metabolic abnormalities, such as visceral obesity, dyslipidaemia and insulin resistance, and may precede the development of obesity and T2D. Further, the presence of obesity and T2D increases the risk of fibrosis progression in MASH. Liver disease and mortality related to MASLD are predicted to continue to rise with the increase in the prevalence of obesity and diabetes, and an ageing population.

As discussed above, MASH is a serious progressive disease with substantial clinical, humanistic, and economic burdens. Still, with liver fibrosis being reversible, the evolution of MASH can be bidirectional, and the progression of MASH could potentially be stabilised or even reversed.

Hitherto, lifestyle changes, including diet and exercise have been considered standard of care. Excess body weight is an important risk factor for the development of MASH and progression of liver fibrosis. Although patients may achieve weight loss through lifestyle intervention, many are unable to maintain their weight loss.

When meeting the criteria for metabolic surgery and in the absence of decompensated cirrhosis, bariatric surgery is an option for people with MASH and has been shown to resolve MASH in around 80% of patients 1 year after surgery. Bariatric surgery, however, is an invasive procedure that remains associated with several major risks, including surgical complications.

Treatments used off-label for the treatment MASH include Vitamin E, pioglitazone and glucagon-like peptide 1 (GLP-1) receptor agonists (RAs).

In summary, MASH is considered a condition with high unmet need, which is also in accordance with EMA's reflection paper stating that a CMA for MASH can be considered. Novo Nordisk considers that semaglutide 2.4 mg for MASH can address this unmet medical need, and the efficacy and safety of semaglutide 2.4 mg are described in the following sections.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

- The benefits to public health of the immediate availability outweigh the risks inherent in the fact that additional data are still required.

The Applicant has explained that, whilst semaglutide or any other GLP-1 RA are currently not approved for the treatment of MASH, the recent AASLD19 and AACE clinical practice guideline recommend considering semaglutide or other GLP-1 RAs for pharmacotherapy of MASH for patients who already have an indication for GLP-1 RAs. The AASLD guideline references semaglutide for the approved indications in T2D and obesity, its cardiometabolic benefits and the ability to improve MASH as shown in phase 1 and 2 clinical trials. In addition, the current EASL guidance recommend maximising the use of GLP-1 RAs for treatment of comorbidities in people with MASH.

In the Applicant's view, the clinical evidence provided from the on-going phase 3 and completed phase 2 trials demonstrated clinically relevant improvements in liver histology and other liver-related parameters as well as benefits on cardiovascular risk and cardiometabolic risk factors, including those related to key MASH-related comorbidities such as obesity and T2D.

In trial 4553 (part 1), the efficacy for the two intermediate endpoints (resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis and improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis) was demonstrated in a co-primary fashion. As supported by retrospective and prospective data and in accordance with available regulatory guidelines, the primary endpoints of the interim evaluation of the phase 3 trial 4553 are likely to predict clinical benefit.

Given the significant unmet need, Novo Nordisk considers that the immediate availability of semaglutide 2.4 mg for treatment of MASH clearly outweighs the risk inherent in the fact that fully comprehensive data, i.e. the validation of the meaningful benefits on clinically relevant liver-related outcomes, are still required.

## 9.6.3.1.2. Discussion on the request for a Conditional marketing authorisation

In regard to the request for conditional Marketing authorisation the rapporteur/CHMP consider the following:

## Positive benefit risk balance

The benefit risk balance is currently considered positive, and the proposed defined target population has been appropriately defined. As per the interim clinical data provided within the procedure, semaglutide has demonstrated a beneficial effect on the intermediate relevant histological endpoints of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis and improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis during current interim. These are thought to reasonably predict clinical outcome in the long-term.

## It is likely that the applicant will be able to provide comprehensive data

Currently, data have been presented at the pre-defined interim stage up to week 72 out of the intended 240 weeks of follow-up for evaluation of clinical endpoints for MASH. Some supportive evidence from other endpoints strengthens these findings. Nevertheless, whether these observed treatment effects will translate in long-term benefit remains to be seen and should be demonstrated by the on-going pivotal study evaluating cirrhosis-free survival at week 240. Despite the known safety profile of semaglutide from existing indications, safety data from the pivotal study 4553 are based on treatment for 72 weeks which is rather limited, and final results of study 4553 after completion of the planned 240 weeks of treatment is expected to provide relevant additional safety data, including data on several safety risks that may persist (like hypoglycaemia) or may increase (like cholelithiasis and acute pancreatitis) during long-term treatment.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Once a marketing authorisation is granted, this could raise a risk to the study integrity, e.g. causing additional drop-out. Also, in the meantime available therapies could alter standard of care and jeopardize primary study estimation. However, the applicant has discussed measures to avoid publication of specific details and data that would pose a risk to the study design and integrity. These have been taken and will continue, to ensure that all recruited patients will remain in the study and include: close monitoring of potential drop-outs, close contact with study stakeholders, and advice and education and training on this aspect. Also, consideration is being given, including in the EPAR, to limiting public dissemination until the end of study. These measures are considered reassuring.  The study is therefore overall considered feasible, and the provision of final study results will provide data post-authorisation for the comprehensiveness of the dossier and is therefore imposed as a specific obligation (SOB) to the CMA.

Additional safety studies are on-going, and it is expected that they will provide relevant information also in relation to the MASH indication: study MTC-22341 is an on-going medullary thyroid carcinoma surveillance study and study NN9535-4447 is an epidemiological assessment of the risk for pancreatic cancer associated with the use of semaglutide. They are both included in the RMP as non-imposed category 3 studies.

## Unmet medical need

According to the EMA reflection paper, MASH is considered a progressive disease with a necroinflammatory phenotype of non-alcoholic fatty liver disease, with the potential of development of cirrhosis and end-stage liver disease (ESLD) with increased risk of hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC). To that end, semaglutide would in principle fulfil an unmet medical need. In addition, a new medicine (resmetirom) has been granted a conditional marketing authorisation by the European Commission for the same indication as the one claimed for Kayshild. While the specific obligations are not yet fully completed, it is not possible to confirm the full benefit of a conditionally authorised product. Nevertheless, semaglutide is a medicinal product with a different mode of action (compared to resmetirom) extending the possibility of different treatment options in the treatment of MASH. Also, the demonstrated extra-hepatic benefits of semaglutide in addressing improvement (in other) cardiometabolic risk factors can be part of these considerations. Therefore, it is still considered that semaglutide would fulfil an unmet medical need to at least the same extent as for the already conditionally authorised product.

## Benefits to public health of the immediate availability outweigh the risks inherent in the fact that additional data are still required

Very recently, another medicinal product for MASH with a comparable target population has been approved. Nevertheless, there is still an unmet medical need for this population as described above and for a part of the intended population, treatment with semaglutide is not yet indicated based on the already approved indications for semaglutide.

In addition, without treatment for MASH, F2/F3 patients are at high risk of disease progression to MASH cirrhosis, which increases the risk for liver-related morbidity and mortality. Semaglutide was superior to placebo on intermediate histological endpoints of resolution of steatohepatitis and no worsening of liver fibrosis, and improvement in liver fibrosis and no worsening of steatohepatitis, thus demonstrating a beneficial effect on MASH disease progression. Finally, the safety profile of semaglutide has been well established, although partly in a different population, which may provide a reasonable prediction of its risks in the current intended population. The benefits to public health of immediate availability of semaglutide to patients with MASH is considered to outweigh the risks although additional data regarding clinically relevant outcomes are still required to render the dataset to be comprehensive.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## 9.6.3.1.3. Conclusions and recommendation on conditional marketing authorisation

As comprehensive data on the product are not available as discussed above, a conditional marketing authorisation was requested by the applicant in the initial submission.

The product falls within the scope of Article 14-a of Regulation (EC) No 726/2004 concerning conditional marketing authorisations, as it aims at the treatment of a life-threatening disease.

The product is considered to fulfil the requirements for a conditional marketing authorisation:

- The benefit-risk balance is positive in the treatment of adults with non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunction-associated steatohepatitis (MASH) with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (fibrosis stages F2 to F3), in conjunction with diet and exercise, as discussed.
- It is likely that the applicant will be able to provide comprehensive data.
- Unmet medical need will be addressed to at least the same extent as for the already conditionally authorised product, as semaglutide is a medicinal product with a different mode of action (compared to the already authorised medicinal product for this indication) extending the possibility of different treatment options in the treatment of MASH, which allows for a relevant contribution to a more individualised treatment approach. In addition, extra-hepatic benefits of semaglutide in addressing improvement (in other) cardiometabolic risk factors have been demonstrated.
- The benefits to public health of the immediate availability outweigh the risks inherent in the fact that additional data are still required. For a part of the intended population, treatment with semaglutide is not covered by the existing indications for semaglutide. Further, the safety profile of semaglutide has been well established, although partly in a different population, which may provide a reasonable prediction of its risks in the current intended population.

The CHMP considers the following measures necessary to address the missing data in the context of conditional marketing authorisation:

Table 49: Specific obligations in relation to the CMA

| Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Due date         |
|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|------------------|
| In order to confirm the efficacy and safety of resmetirom in adults with non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunction-associated steatohepatitis (MASH) with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (fibrosis stages F2 to F3), the MAH shall submit the final results of NN9931-4553 (ESSENCE), a phase III, double-blind, randomized, placebo-controlled study. | 31 December 2029 |

## 9.7. Benefit-risk conclusions

## 9.7.1. Final CHMP conclusions

The CHMP considered that the overall benefit /risk balance of Kayshild in the indication treatment of adults with non-cirrhotic metabolic dysfunction-associated steatohepatitis (MASH) with moderate to advanced liver fibrosis (fibrosis stages F2 to F3), in conjunction with diet and exercise , is positive.
